2:22:1296:0:14:72:279:700:12:Times:12:Times:?:Quantitative Easing and Financial Stability
2:23:1339:14:14:72:164:686:12:Times:12:Times:?:Michael Woodford
2:24:1355:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 22285
2:25:1383:14:14:72:121:658:12:Times:12:Times:?:May 2016
2:26:1391:14:28:72:157:644:12:Times:12:Times:?:JEL No. E44,E52
2:27:1406:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:A:ABSTRACT
2:28:1414:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:?:The  massive  expansion  of  central-bank  balance  sheets  in  response  to  recent  crises  raises 
2:29:1515:14:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:important questions about the effects of such "quantitative easing" policies, both their effects on 
2:30:1614:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:financial  conditions and  on  aggregate  demand  (the  intended  effects  of  the  policies),  and  their 
2:31:1720:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:possible  collateral  effects on  financial  stability.  The  present  paper  compares  three  alternative 
2:32:1826:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:dimensions  of  central  bank  policy —  conventional  interest-rate  policy,  increases  in  the  central 
2:33:1932:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:bank's  supply  of  safe  (monetary)  liabilities, and  macroprudential  policy  (possibly  implemented 
2:34:2035:14:14:71:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:through  discretionary  changes  in  reserve  requirements) —  showing  in  the  context  of  a  simple 
2:35:2138:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:intertemporal  general-equilibrium  model  why  they  are  logically independent  dimensions  of 
2:36:2234:14:14:71:546:476:12:Times:12:Times:?:variation  in  policy,  and  how  they  jointly  determine  financial  conditions, aggregate  demand,  and 
2:37:2340:14:14:71:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:?:the  severity  of  the  risks  associated  with  a  funding  crisis  in  the  banking  sector. In  the  proposed 
2:38:2452:14:14:71:546:448:12:Times:12:Times:?:model, each of the three dimensions of policy can be used independently to influence aggregate 
2:39:2546:14:14:71:545:434:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:?:demand,  and  in  each  case  a  more  stimulative  policy  also  increases  financial  stability  risk. 
2:40:2650:14:14:71:545:420:12:Times:12:Times:?:However,  the  policies  are  not  equivalent,  and  in  particular  the  relative  magnitudes  of  the  two 
2:41:2759:14:14:71:545:406:12:Times:12:Times:?:kinds of effects are not the same. Quantitative easing policies increase financial stability risk (in 
2:42:2860:14:14:72:546:392:12:Times:12:Times:?:the absence of an offsetting tightening of macroprudential policy), but they actually increase such 
2:43:2959:14:14:72:546:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:risk  less  than either  of  the  other  two  policies,  relative  to  the  magnitude  of  aggregate  demand 
2:44:3067:14:14:72:546:364:12:Times:12:Times:?:stimulus;  and  a  combination of  expansion  of  the  central  bank's  balance  sheet  with  a  suitable 
2:45:3172:14:14:72:546:350:12:Times:12:Times:?:tightening  of  macroprudential  policy can  have  a  net  expansionary  effect  on  aggregate  demand 
2:46:3274:14:14:72:545:336:12:Times:12:Times:?:with no increased risk to financial stability. This suggests that quantitative easing policies may be 
2:47:3375:14:14:71:545:322:12:Times:12:Times:?:useful  as  an  approach  to  aggregate  demand  management not  only  when  the  zero  lower  bound 
2:48:3475:14:14:71:545:308:12:Times:12:Times:?:precludes  further  use  of  conventional  interest-rate  policy,  but also  when  it  is  not  desirable  to 
2:49:3584:14:42:71:392:294:12:Times:12:Times:?:further reduce interest rates because of financial stability concerns.
2:50:3654:42:14:71:163:252:12:Times:12:Times:?:Michael Woodford
2:51:3670:14:14:71:197:238:12:Times:12:Times:?:Department of Economics
2:52:3693:14:14:71:172:224:12:Times:12:Times:?:Columbia University
2:53:3712:14:14:71:168:210:12:Times:12:Times:?:420 W. 118th Street
2:54:3731:14:14:71:178:196:12:Times:12:Times:?:New York, NY 10027
2:55:3749:14:14:71:123:182:12:Times:12:Times:?:and NBER
2:56:3757:14:0:71:189:168:12:Times:12:Times:?:mw2230@columbia.edu
3:57:3776:0:18:111:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Since  the  global  financial  crisis  of  2008-09,  many  of  the  leading  central  banks
3:58:3867:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have  dramatically  increased  the  size  of  their  balance  sheets,  and  also  have  shifted
3:59:3962:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the composition of the assets that they hold, toward greater holdings of longer-term
3:60:4046:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:securities (as well as toward assets that are riskier in other respects).  While many
3:61:4131:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have hailed these policies as contributing significantly to contain the degree of damage
3:62:4219:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to both the countries’ financial systems and real economies resulting from the collapse
3:63:4306:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of confidence in certain types of risky assets, the policies have also been and remain
3:64:4392:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:quite controversial.  One of the concerns raised by skeptics has been the suggestion
3:65:4476:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that such “quantitative easing” by central banks may have been supporting countries’
3:66:4560:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:banking systems and aggregate demand only by encouraging risk-taking by ultimate
3:67:4640:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:borrowers and by financial intermediaries of a kind that increases the risk of precisely
3:68:4728:17:17:93:513:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the sort of destructive financial crisis that had led these policies to be introduced.
3:69:4814:17:18:111:525:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The most basic argument for suspecting that such policies create risks to financial
3:70:4897:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stability is simply that, according to proponents of these policies in the central banks
3:71:4985:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(e.g., Bernanke, 2012), they represent alternative means of achieving the same kind
3:72:5068:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of relaxation of financial conditions that would under more ordinary circumstances
3:73:5150:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be achieved by lowering the central bank’s operating target for short-term interest
3:74:5233:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rates — but a means that continues to be available even when short-term nominal
3:75:5312:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:interest  rates  have  already  reached  their  effective  lower  bound,  and  so  cannot  be
3:76:5405:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:lowered to provide further stimulus.  If one believes that cuts in short-term interest
3:77:5491:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rates have as a collateral effect — or perhaps even as the main channel through which
3:78:5576:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:they affect aggregate demand, as argued by Adrian and Shin (2010) — an increase
3:79:5655:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the degree to which intermediaries take more highly leveraged positions in risky
3:80:5738:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets, increasing the likelihood of and/or severity of a potential financial crisis, then
3:81:5828:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:one might suppose that to the extent that quantitative easing policies are effective
3:82:5912:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in relaxing financial conditions in order to stimulate aggregate demand, they should
3:83:5996:17:17:93:317:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:similarly increase risks to financial stability.
3:84:6044:17:18:111:525:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:One might go further and argue that such policies relax financial conditions by
3:85:6123:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increasing  the  supply  of  central-bank  reserves,1and  one  might  suppose  that  such
3:86:6212:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an  increase  in  the  availability  of  reserves  matters  for  financial  conditions  precisely
3:87:6309:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:because it relaxes a constraint on the extent to which private financial intermediaries
3:88:6396:18:18:107:524:169:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:1The  term  “quantitative  easing,”  originally  introduced  by  the  Bank  of  Japan  to  describe  the
3:89:6500:18:15:93:524:151:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:policy that it adopted in 2001 in attempt to stem the deflationary slump that Japan had suffered in
3:90:6599:15:14:93:524:136:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the aftermath of the collapse of an asset bubble in the early 1990s, refers precisely to the intention to
3:91:6704:14:14:93:524:122:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:increase the monetary base (and hence, it was hoped, the money supply more broadly) by increasing
3:92:6801:14:31:93:190:108:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the supply of reserves.
3:93:6824:31:0:299:305:77:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:?:1
4:94:6825:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can issue money-like liabilities (that are subject to reserve requirements) as a way
4:95:6909:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of financing their acquisition of more risky and less liquid assets, as in the model of
4:96:6996:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Stein (2012).  Under this view of the mechanism by which quantitative easing works,
4:97:7079:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:one might suppose that it should be even more inevitably linked to an increase in
4:98:7160:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability risk than expansionary interest-rate policy (which, after all, might
4:99:7248:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:also  increase  aggregate  demand  through  channels  that  do  not  rely  upon  increased
4:100:7338:17:18:93:205:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risk-taking by banks).
4:101:7360:18:17:111:525:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally,  some  may  be  particularly  suspicious  of  quantitative  easing  policies  on
4:102:7449:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the ground that these policies,  unlike conventional interest-rate policy,  relax finan-
4:103:7537:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cial conditions primarily by reducing the risk premia earned by holding longer-term
4:104:7620:18:17:93:525:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:securities, rather than by lowering the expected path of the risk-free rate.2Such a
4:105:7703:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:departure  from  the  normal  historical  pattern  of  risk  premia  as  a  result  of  massive
4:106:7798:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central-bank purchases may seem a cause for alarm.  If one thinks that the premia
4:107:7879:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that exist when market pricing is not “distorted” by the central bank’s intervention
4:108:7963:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:provide an important signal of the degree of risk that exists in the marketplace, one
4:109:8048:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:might fear that central-bank actions that suppress this signal — not by actually re-
4:110:8132:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ducing the underlying risks, but only by preventing them from being reflected so fully
4:111:8218:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in market prices — run the danger of distorting perceptions of risk in a way that will
4:112:8304:17:18:93:255:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:encourage excessive risk-taking.
4:113:8336:18:17:111:525:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The present paper considers the extent to which these are valid grounds for concern
4:114:8419:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:about the use of this policy tool by central banks, by analyzing further the mechanisms
4:115:8506:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:just sketched, in the context of an explicit model of the way in which quantitative
4:116:8589:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing policies influence financial conditions, and the way in which monetary policies
4:117:8675:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:more generally affect the incentives of financial intermediaries to engage in maturity
4:118:8761:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and liquidity transformation of a kind that increases the risk of financial crisis.  It
4:119:8848:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:argues, in fact, that the concerns just raised are of little merit.  But it does not reach
4:120:8938:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this conclusion by challenging the view that quantitative easing policies can indeed
4:121:9022:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effectively relax financial conditions (and so achieve effects on aggregate demand that
4:122:9109:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are similar to the effects of conventional interest-rate policy); nor does it deny that
4:123:9196:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risks to financial stability are an appropriate concern of monetary policy deliberations,
4:124:9285:17:19:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:or that expansionary interest-rate policy tends to increase such risks (among other
4:125:9368:19:18:107:524:168:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:2Again see Bernanke (2012) for discussion of this view of how the policies work, though he also
4:126:9463:18:14:93:524:150:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:discusses the possibility of effects of quantitative easing that result from central-bank actions being
4:127:9566:14:0:93:404:136:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:taken to signal different intentions regarding future interest-rate policy.
5:128:9642:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effects).  The model developed here is one in which risk-taking by the financial sector
5:129:9729:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can easily be excessive (in the sense that a restriction on banks’ ability to engage in
5:130:9816:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:liquidity transformation to the degree that they choose to under laissez-faire would
5:131:9900:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:raise welfare);  in which, when that is true, a reduction in short-term interest rates
5:132:9986:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:through central-bank action will worsen the problem by making it even more tempting
5:133:10069:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for  banks  to  finance  acquisitions  of  risky,  illiquid  assets  by  issuing  short-term  safe
5:134:10167:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:liabilities; and in which the purchase of longer-term and/or risky assets by the central
5:135:10255:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank,  financed  by  creating  additional  reserves  (or  other  short-term  safe  liabilities,
5:136:10350:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:such as reverse repos or central-bank bills, that would also be useful in facilitating
5:137:10436:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:transactions),  will  indeed  loosen  financial  conditions,  with  an  effect  on  aggregate
5:138:10529:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand that is similar, though not identical to, the effect of a reduction in the central
5:139:10618:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank’s operating target for its policy rate.  Nonetheless, we show that quantitative
5:140:10702:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing policies should not increase risks to financial stability, and should instead tend
5:141:10791:18:17:93:174:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to reduce them.
5:142:10806:17:17:111:525:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The reason for this different conclusion hinges on our conception of the sources
5:143:10886:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the kind of financial fragility that allowed a crisis of the kind just experienced to
5:144:10974:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:occur, and the way in which monetary policy can affect the incentives to create a more
5:145:11060:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:fragile financial structure.  In our view, the fragility that led to the recent crisis was
5:146:11150:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:greatly enhanced by the notable increase in maturity and liquidity transformation in
5:147:11234:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the financial sector in the years immediately prior to the crisis (Brunnermeier, 2009;
5:148:11320:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Adrian and Shin, 2010) — in particular, the significant increase in funding of financial
5:149:11408:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:intermediaries by issuance of collateralized short-term debt, such as repos (financing
5:150:11494:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investment banks) or asset-backed commercial paper (issued by SIVs). Such financing
5:151:11577:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is relatively inexpensive, in the sense that investors will hold such instruments even
5:152:11663:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:when they promise a relatively low yield, because of the assurance they provide that
5:153:11747:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the investor can be sure of payment and can withdraw their funds at any time on short
5:154:11832:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:notice if desired.  But too much of it is dangerous, because it exposes the leveraged
5:155:11917:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:institution to funding risk, which may require abrupt de-leveraging through a “fire
5:156:12000:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sale”  of  relatively  illiquid  assets.   The  sudden  need  to  sell  relatively  illiquid  assets
5:157:12100:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in order to cover a shortfall of funding can substantially depress the price of those
5:158:12185:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets,  requiring  even  more  de-leveraging  and  leading  to  a  “margin  spiral”  of  the
5:159:12278:18:17:93:524:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:kind described by Shleifer and Vishny (1992, 2010) and Brunnermeier and Pederson
5:160:12358:17:17:93:129:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(2009).
5:161:12365:17:0:111:525:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:It  is  important  to  ask  why  such  fragile  financial  structures  should  arise  as  an
6:162:12458:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium phenomenon, in order to understand how monetary policy may increase
6:163:12537:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:or decrease the likely degree of fragility.  According to the perspective that we adopt
6:164:12624:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:here, investors are attracted to the short-term safe liabilities created by banks or other
6:165:12714:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial  intermediaries  because  assets  with  a  value  that  is  completely  certain  are
6:166:12808:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:more widely accepted as a means of payment.3If an insufficient quantity of such safe
6:167:12892:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets are supplied by the government (through means that we discuss further below),
6:168:12976:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investors will pay a “money premium” for privately-issued short-term safe instruments
6:169:13061:18:17:93:525:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:with this feature, as documented by Greenwoodet al.(2010), Krishnamurthy and
6:170:13137:17:17:93:525:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Vissing-Jorgensen (2012),  and Carlsonet al.(2014).  This provides banks with an
6:171:13217:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:incentive to obtain a larger fraction of their financing in this way.  Moreover, they may
6:172:13306:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:choose an excessive amount of this kind of financing, despite the funding risk to which
6:173:13393:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:it exposes them, because each individual bank fails to internalize the effects of their
6:174:13480:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:collective financing decisions on the degree to which asset prices will be depressed in
6:175:13567:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the event of a “fire sale.”  This gives rise to a pecuniary externality,  as a result of
6:176:13655:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:which excessive risk is taken in equilibrium (Lorenzoni, 2008;  Jeanne and Korinek,
6:177:13738:17:18:93:188:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:2010; Stein, 2012).
6:178:13757:18:17:111:525:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Conventional  monetary  policy,  which  cuts  short-term  nominal  interest  rates  in
6:179:13843:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:response to an aggregate demand shortfall, can arguably exacerbate this problem, as
6:180:13926:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:low market yields on short-term safe instruments will further increase the incentive
6:181:14010:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for private issuance of liabilities of this kind (Adrian and Shin, 2010;  Giavazzi and
6:182:14096:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Giovannini, 2012).  The question of primary concern in this paper is, do quantitative
6:183:14181:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing policies, pursued as a means of providing economic stimulus when conventional
6:184:14265:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy is constrained by the lower bound on short-term nominal interest
6:185:14345:17:17:93:393:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rates, increase financial stability risks for a similar reason?
6:186:14408:17:18:111:525:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In the model proposed here, quantitative easing policies lower the equilibrium real
6:187:14491:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:yield on longer-term and risky government liabilities, just as a cut in the central bank’s
6:188:14581:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:target for the short-term riskless rate will, and this relaxation of financial conditions
6:189:14670:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:has a similar expansionary effect on aggregate demand in both cases.  Nonetheless,
6:190:14752:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the consequences for financial stability are not the same.  In the case of conventional
6:191:14839:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy, a reduction in the riskless rate lowers the equilibrium yield on risky
6:192:14926:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets  as  well  because,  if  it  did  not,  the  increased  spread  between  the  two  yields
6:193:15022:18:18:107:524:169:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:3The role of non-state-contingent payoffs in allowing an asset to be widely acceptable as a means
6:194:15119:18:15:93:524:151:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of payment is stressed in particular by Gorton and Pennacchi (2010), and in recent discussions such
6:195:15218:15:0:93:355:136:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:as Gorton (2010) and Gorton, Lewellen and Metrick (2012).
7:196:15276:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:would  provide  an  increased  incentive  for  maturity  and  liquidity  transformation  on
7:197:15367:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the part of banks, which they pursue until a point at which the spread has decreased
7:198:15451:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(because  of  diminishing  returns  to  further  investment  in  risky  assets)  to  where  it
7:199:15545:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is  again  balanced  by  the  risks  associated  with  overly  leveraged  investment.   (This
7:200:15638:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:occurs, in equilibrium, partly through a reduction in the degree to which the spread
7:201:15722:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increases — which means that the expected return on risky assets is reduced — and
7:202:15803:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:partly  through  an  increase  in  the  risk  of  a  costly  “fire  sale”  liquidation  of  assets.)
7:203:15903:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In the case of quantitative easing, instead, the equilibrium return on risky assets is
7:204:15989:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reduced, but in this case through a reduction, rather than an increase in the spread
7:205:16073:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:between the two yields.  The “money premium,” which results from a scarcity of safe
7:206:16156:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets, should be reduced if the central-bank asset purchases increase the supply of
7:207:16240:17:17:93:525:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f6:B:safe assets to the public, as argued by Caballero and Farhi (2013) and Carlsonet al.
7:208:16324:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(2014).  Hence the incentives for creation of a more fragile financial structure are not
7:209:16412:18:17:93:425:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increased as much by expansionary monetary policy of this kind.
7:210:16475:17:17:111:525:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The idea that quantitative easing policies, when pursued as an additional means
7:211:16554:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of stimulus when the risk-free rate is at the zero lower bound, should increase risks to
7:212:16642:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability because they are analogous to an expansionary policy that relaxes
7:213:16727:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reserve  requirements  on  private  issuers  of  money-like  liabilities  is  also  based  on  a
7:214:16823:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:flawed analogy.  It is true, in the model of endogenous financial stability risk presented
7:215:16913:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:here,  that  a  relaxation  of  a  reserve  requirement  proportional  to  banks’  issuance  of
7:216:17008:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:short-term  safe  liabilities  will  (in  the  case  that  the  constraint  binds)  increase  the
7:217:17105:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:degree to which excessive liquidity transformation occurs.  And it is also true that in
7:218:17192:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a conventional textbook account of the way in which monetary policy affects financial
7:219:17277:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:conditions,  an  increase  in  the  supply  of  reserves  by  the  central  bank  relaxes  the
7:220:17371:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraint  on  banks’  issuance  of  additional  money-like  liabilities  (“inside  money”)
7:221:17463:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:implied  by  the  reserve  requirement,  so  that  the  means  through  which  the  central
7:222:17554:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank  implements  a  reduction  in  the  riskless  short-term  interest  rate  is  essentially
7:223:17648:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equivalent to a reduction in the reduction in the reserve requirement.  However, this
7:224:17733:18:17:93:525:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:isnota channel through which quantitative easing policies can be effective, when the
7:225:17817:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risk-free rate has already fallen to zero (or more generally, to the level of interest paid
7:226:17908:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on reserves).  For in such a case, reserves are necessarily already in sufficiently great
7:227:17997:18:17:93:524:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:supply for banks to be satiated in reserves, so that the opportunity cost of holding
7:228:18081:17:17:93:524:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:them must fall to zero in order for the existing supply to be voluntarily held.  Under
7:229:18167:17:0:93:524:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:such  circumstances  (which  is  to  say,  those  existing  in  countries  like  the  US  since
8:230:18263:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the end of 2008), banks’ reserve requirements have already ceased to constrain their
8:231:18347:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:behavior.  Hence, to the extent that quantitative easing policies are of any use at the
8:232:18434:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:zero lower bound on short-term interest rates, their effects cannot occur through this
8:233:18520:17:18:93:193:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:traditional channel.
8:234:18540:18:17:111:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In  the  model  presented  here,  quantitative  easingiseffective  at  the  zero  lower
8:235:18627:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bound (or more generally, even in the absence of reserve requirements, or under cir-
8:236:18711:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cumstances where there is already satiation in reserves); this is because an increase
8:237:18796:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in  the  supply  of  safe  assets  (through  issuance  of  additional  short-term  safe  liabili-
8:238:18893:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ties  by  the  central  bank,  used  to  purchase  assets  that  are  not  equally  money-like)
8:239:18988:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reduces the equilibrium “money premium.”  But whereas a relaxation of a binding
8:240:19067:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reserve requirement would increase banks’ issuance of short-term safe liabilities (and
8:241:19153:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:hence  financial  stability  risk),  a  reduction  in  the  “money  premium”  should  reduce
8:242:19245:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:their issuance of such liabilities, so that financial stability risk should if anything be
8:243:19335:18:17:93:136:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reduced.
8:244:19343:17:17:111:525:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The idea that a reduction in risk premia as a result of central-bank balance-sheet
8:245:19425:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policy should imply a greater danger of excessive risk-taking is similarly mistaken.
8:246:19509:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In  the  model  presented  here,  quantitative  easing  achieves  its  effects  (both  on  the
8:247:19603:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium required return on risky assets and on aggregate demand) by lowering
8:248:19683:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the equilibrium risk premium — that is, the spread between the required return on
8:249:19764:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risky assets and the riskless rate.  But this does not imply the creation of conditions
8:250:19851:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:under which it should be more tempting for banks to take on greater risk.  To the
8:251:19932:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:contrary, the existence of a smaller spread between the expected return on risky assets
8:252:20019:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and the risk-free rate makes it less tempting to finance purchases of risky assets by
8:253:20104:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:issuing safe, highly liquid short-term liabilities that need pay only the riskless rate.
8:254:20192:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Hence again a correct analysis implies that quantitative easing policies should increase
8:255:20280:18:17:93:324:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability, rather than threatening it.
8:256:20328:17:17:111:525:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The  remainder  of  the  paper  develops  these  points  in  the  context  of  an  explicit
8:257:20419:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:intertemporal monetary equilibrium model, in which it is possible to clearly trace the
8:258:20505:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:general-equilibrium determinants of risk premia, the way in which they are affected by
8:259:20591:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:both interest-rate policy and the central bank’s balance sheet, and the consequences
8:260:20675:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for the endogenous capital structure decisions of banks.  Section 1 presents the struc-
8:261:20762:18:17:93:524:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ture of the model, and section 2 then derives the conditions that must link the various
8:262:20849:17:17:93:524:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:endogenous prices and quantities in an intertemporal equilibrium.  Section 3 considers
8:263:20935:17:0:93:524:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the effects of alternative balance-sheet policies on equilibrium variables, focusing on
9:264:21023:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the case of a stationary long-run equilibrium with flexible prices.  Section 4 compares
9:265:21110:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the  ways  in  which  quantitative  easing  and  adjustments  of  reserve  requirements  af-
9:266:21202:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:fect banks’ financing decisions.  Finally, section 5 compares (somewhat more briefly)
9:267:21287:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the short-run effects of both conventional monetary policy, quantitative easing, and
9:268:21371:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:macroprudential policy in the presence of nominal rigidities that allow conventional
9:269:21455:17:44:93:518:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy to affect the degree of real economic activity.  Section 6 concludes.
9:270:21540:44:29:93:524:576:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:F:1    A Monetary Equilibrium Model with Fire Sales
9:271:21589:29:18:93:524:547:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This section develops a simple model of monetary equilibrium, in which it is possible
9:272:21674:18:17:93:524:529:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:simultaneously to consider the effects of the central bank’s balance sheet on financial
9:273:21761:17:17:93:524:512:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:conditions (most notably, the equilibrium spread between the expected rate of return
9:274:21845:17:18:93:524:495:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on risky assets and the risk-free rate of interest) and the way in which private banks’
9:275:21932:18:17:93:524:477:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financing decisions can increase risks to financial stability.  An important goal of the
9:276:22020:17:17:93:524:460:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:analysis is to present a sufficiently explicit model of the objectives and constraints
9:277:22106:17:18:93:524:443:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of individual actors to allow welfare analysis of the equilibria associated with alter-
9:278:22193:18:17:93:524:425:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:native policies that is based on the degree of satisfaction of the individual objectives
9:279:22281:17:17:93:524:408:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:underlying  the  behavior  assumed  in  the  model,  as  in  the  modern  theory  of  public
9:280:22373:17:18:93:524:391:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:finance, rather than judging alternative equilibria on the basis of some more ad hoc
9:281:22457:18:17:93:143:373:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:criterion.4
9:282:22468:17:18:111:525:356:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Risks  to  financial  stability  are  modeled  using  a  slightly  adapted  version  of  the
9:283:22560:18:17:93:524:338:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:model proposed by Stein (2012).  The Stein model is a three-period model in which
9:284:22641:17:17:93:524:321:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:banks finance their investments in risky assets in the first period; a crisis may occur in
9:285:22731:17:18:93:524:304:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the second period, in which banks are unable to roll over their short-term financing
9:286:22815:18:17:93:524:286:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and  as  a  result  may  have  to  sell  illiquid  risky  assets  in  a  “fire  sale”;  and  in  the
9:287:22915:17:17:93:524:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:third period, the ultimate value of the risky assets is determined.  The present model
9:288:23001:17:18:93:524:252:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:incorporates this model of financial contracting and occasional fire sales of assets into
9:289:23090:18:17:93:524:234:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a fairly standard intertemporal general-equilibrium model of the demand for money-
9:290:23172:17:17:93:524:217:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:like  assets,  the  “cash-in-advance”  model  of  Lucas  and  Stokey  (1987).   In  this  way,
9:291:23266:17:18:93:524:200:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the premium earned by money-like assets, that is treated as an exogenous parameter
9:292:23348:18:18:93:524:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in Stein (2012),  can be endogenized,  and the effects of central-bank policy on this
9:293:23433:18:18:107:524:164:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:4The proposed framework is further developed in Sergeyev (2016), which considers the interaction
9:294:23529:18:14:93:524:146:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:between conventional monetary policy and country-specific macroprudential policies in a currency
9:295:23625:14:0:93:120:132:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:union.
10:296:23632:0:39:93:515:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:variable can be analyzed, and through this the consequences for financial stability.
10:297:23716:39:25:93:291:668:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:1.1    Elements of the Model
10:298:23744:25:17:93:524:643:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Like most general-equilibrium models of monetary exchange, the Lucas and Stokey
10:299:23823:17:17:93:524:626:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(1987) model is an infinite-horizon model, in which the willingness of sellers to accept
10:300:23911:17:18:93:524:609:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central-bank liabilities as payment for real goods and services in any period depends
10:301:23996:18:17:93:524:591:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on the expectation of being able to use those instruments as a means of payment in
10:302:24078:17:17:93:524:574:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:further  transactions  in  future  periods.   The  state  space  of  the  model  is  kept  small
10:303:24174:17:18:93:524:557:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(allowing  a  straightforward  characterization  of  equilibrium,  despite  random  distur-
10:304:24265:18:17:93:524:539:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bances each period) by assuming a representative household structure; the two sides
10:305:24348:17:17:93:524:522:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of each transaction involving payment using cash are assumed to be two members of
10:306:24429:17:18:93:524:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a household unit with a common objective, that can be thought of as a “worker” and
10:307:24511:18:17:93:524:487:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a “shopper.”  During each period,  the worker and shopper from a given household
10:308:24591:17:17:93:524:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have separate budget constraints (so that cash received by the worker as payment for
10:309:24675:17:18:93:524:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the sale of produced goods cannot be immediately used by the shopper to purchase
10:310:24755:18:17:93:524:435:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods, in the same market), as is necessary for the “cash-in-advance” constraint to
10:311:24838:17:17:93:524:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:matter; but at the end of the period, their funds are again pooled in a single house-
10:312:24923:17:18:93:524:401:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:hold budget constraint (so that only the asset positions of households, that are all
10:313:25007:18:17:93:253:383:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:identical, matter at this point).
10:314:25040:17:17:111:525:366:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We shall employ a similar device, but further increasing the number of distinct
10:315:25119:17:18:93:524:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:roles for different members of the household, in order to introduce additional kinds
10:316:25203:18:17:93:524:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of  financial  constraints  into  the  model,  while  retaining  the  convenience  of  a  repre-
10:317:25299:17:17:93:524:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sentative household.  We suppose that each infinite-lived household is made of four
10:318:25382:17:18:93:524:297:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:members with different roles during the period:  a “worker” who supplies the inputs
10:319:25465:18:17:93:524:279:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:used to produce all final goods, and receives the income from the sale of these goods;
10:320:25551:17:17:93:524:262:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a “shopper” who purchases “regular goods” for consumption by the household, and
10:321:25630:17:18:93:524:245:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:who holds the household’s cash balance, for use in such transactions; a “banker” who
10:322:25714:18:17:93:524:227:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:buys  risky  durable  goods,  and  issues  short-term  safe  liabilities  in  order  to  finance
10:323:25810:17:17:93:524:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:some of these purchases; and an “investor” who purchases “special” final goods, and
10:324:25893:17:18:93:524:193:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can also bid for the risky durables sold by bankers in the event of a fire sale.5As
10:325:25976:18:18:107:524:175:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:5The distinction between bankers, investors, and worker/shopper pairs corresponds to the dis-
10:326:26069:18:14:93:524:157:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:tinction in the roles of “bankers,” “patient investors,” and “households” in the model of Stein (2012).
10:327:26172:14:15:93:524:143:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:In the Stein model, these three types of agents are distinct individuals with no sharing of resources
10:328:26273:15:0:93:524:128:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:among them, rather than members of a single (larger) household; the device of having them pool
11:329:26368:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the Lucas-Stokey model,  the different household members have separate budget
11:330:26448:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraints during the period (which is the significance of referring to them as differ-
11:331:26536:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ent people), but pool their budgets at the end of each period in a single household
11:332:26619:17:18:93:186:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:budget constraint.
11:333:26637:18:17:111:525:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Four types of final goods are produced each period: durable goods and three types
11:334:26718:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of non-durable goods, called “cash goods,” “credit goods,” and “special goods.”  In
11:335:26801:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:addition,  we  suppose  that  workers  also  produce  intermediate  “investment  goods”
11:336:26888:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that  are  used  as  an  input  in  the  production  of  durable  goods.   Both  “cash”  and
11:337:26980:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:“credit” goods are purchased by shoppers; the distinction between the two types of
11:338:27062:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods is taken from Lucas and Stokey (1987), where the possibility of substitution
11:339:27144:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by  consumers  between  the  two  types  of  goods  (one  subject  to  the  cash-in-advance
11:340:27235:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraint, the other not) allows the demand for real cash balances to vary with the
11:341:27319:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:size of the liquidity premium (opportunity cost of holding cash), for a given level of
11:342:27405:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:planned real expenditure.  This margin of substitution also results in a distortion in
11:343:27491:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the  allocation  of  resources  that  depends  on  the  size  of  the  liquidity  premium,  and
11:344:27586:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we wish to take this distortion into account when considering the welfare effects of
11:345:27670:18:17:93:365:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:changing the size of the central bank’s balance sheet.
11:346:27724:17:17:111:525:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The introduction of “special goods” purchased only by the investor provides an
11:347:27802:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:alternative use for the funds available to the investor,  so that the amount that in-
11:348:27887:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:vestors will spend on risky durables in a fire sale depends on how low the price of
11:349:27970:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the durables falls.6The produced “durable goods” in our model play the role of the
11:350:28052:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risky investment projects in the model of Stein (2012):  they require an initial outlay
11:351:28139:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of resources, financed by bankers, in order to allow the production of something that
11:352:28224:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:may or may not yield a return later.  The device of referring separately to investment
11:353:28310:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods and to the durable goods produced from them allows us to treat investment
11:354:28389:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods as perfect substitutes for cash or credit goods on the production side, allowing
11:355:28475:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a simple specification of workers’ disutility of supplying more output, without having
11:356:28561:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:also to treat durable goods as perfect substitutes for those goods, which would not
11:357:28644:18:21:93:398:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:allow the relative price of durables to rise in a credit boom.
11:358:28706:21:14:93:524:200:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:assets at the end of each “period” is not needed to simplify the model dynamics, because the model
11:359:28804:14:15:93:524:186:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:simply ends when the end of the first and only “period” is reached (in the sense in which the term
11:360:28902:15:14:93:524:171:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:“period” is used in this model).  Note that in the present model, the representative household device
11:361:29003:14:9:93:394:157:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:also allows more unambiguous welfare comparisons among equilibria.
11:362:29069:9:18:107:524:148:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:6The opportunity of spending on purchases of special goods plays the same role in our model as
11:363:29163:18:0:93:461:130:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:the possibility of investment in “late-arriving projects” in the model of Stein (2012).
12:364:29251:0:18:111:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:All of the members of a given household are assumed to act so as to maximize a

12:381:30353:17:17:93:524:430:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that both cash and credit goods are normal goods, in the sense that it will be optimal

13:420:32437:17:17:93:524:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be worthless.  Finally, in subperiod 3, the value of the risky durables is learned.  In
13:421:32524:17:18:93:524:318:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:both of the states labeled “no asset collapse,” a unit of the durable good produces
13:422:32607:18:17:93:524:300:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:one unit of services, while in the “asset collapse” state (that occurs with probability
13:423:32694:17:17:93:525:283:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:1−q, conditional on the crisis state being reached), durables provide no service flow.
13:424:32780:17:18:111:525:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The various types of goods are produced and sold in sub-period 2.  The markets in
13:425:32861:18:17:93:524:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:which the different goods are sold differ in the means of payment that are accepted.
13:426:32945:17:17:93:524:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:It is assumed, as in Lucas and Stokey (1987), that “cash goods” are sold only for cash
13:427:33031:17:18:93:524:214:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that is transferred from the buyer to the seller at that time; the cash balances used for
13:428:33120:18:17:93:524:196:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this purpose must have been acquired in sub-period 1 by the household to which that
13:429:33203:17:17:93:524:179:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shopper belongs.  (The liquidity premium associated with cash is thus determined in
13:430:33286:17:18:93:524:162:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the exchange of cash for other financial claims in subperiod 1.)  “Credit goods” are
13:431:33370:18:0:93:524:144:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:instead sold to shoppers on credit; this means (as in Lucas and Stokey) that accounts
14:432:33457:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are settled between buyers and sellers only at the end of the period, at which point
14:433:33541:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the various household members have again pooled their resources, so that charges by
14:434:33624:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shoppers  during  the  period  can  be  paid  out  of  the  income  received  by  workers  for
14:435:33718:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods sold during that same period.  The only constraint on the amount of credit of
14:436:33801:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this kind that a household can draw upon is assumed to be determined by a no-Ponzi
14:437:33883:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:condition (that is,  the requirement that a household’s debts be able to be paid off
14:438:33967:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:eventually out of future income,  rather than rolled over indefinitely).  “Investment
14:439:34052:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods” are sold on credit in the same way.  “Special goods” are also assumed to be
14:440:34134:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sold on credit, but in this case, the amount of credit that investors can draw upon is
14:441:34220:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:limited by the size of the line of credit arranged for them in subperiod 1. In particular,
14:442:34310:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:it is assumed that a given credit limit must be negotiated by the household before
14:443:34392:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:it is learned whether a crisis will occur in subperiod 2, and thus whether investors
14:444:34476:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:will have an opportunity to bid on “fire sale” assets.  The existence of the non-state-
14:445:34563:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:contingent  credit  limit  for  purchases  by  investors  (both  their  purchases  of  special
14:446:34657:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods and their purchases of risky durables liquidated by the bankers in a fire sale)
14:447:34742:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is important in order to capture the idea that only a limited quantity of funds can
14:448:34825:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be mobilized (by potential buyers with the expertise required to evaluate the assets)
14:449:34910:17:17:93:291:412:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:to bid on the assets sold in a fire sale.9
14:450:34952:17:18:111:525:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The nature of the “cash” that can be used to purchase cash goods requires further
14:451:35033:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:comment.  Unlike Lucas and Stokey, we do not assume that only monetary liabilities
14:452:35115:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the government constitute “cash” that is acceptable as a means of payment in this
14:453:35199:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:market.   We  instead  identify  “cash”  with  the  class  of  short-term  safe  instruments
14:454:35291:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(STSIs) discussed by Carlsonet al.(2014) in the case of the U.S.,  which includes
14:455:35372:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:U.S. Treasury bills (and not simply monetary liabilities of the Federal Reserve), and
14:456:35457:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:certain types of collateralized short-term debt of private financial institutions.  The
14:457:35544:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assumption that only these assets can be used to purchase cash goods is intended to
14:458:35627:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stand in for the convenience provided by these special instruments, that accounts for
14:459:35712:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:their lower equilibrium yields relative to the short-period holding returns on other
14:460:35796:18:18:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets.10The fact that all assets of this type, whether issued by the government (or
14:461:35880:18:18:107:524:203:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:9In the model of Stein (2012), this limit is ensured by assuming that the “patient investors” have
14:462:35978:18:15:93:524:185:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:a budget that is fixed as a parameter of the model.  Here we endogenize this budget, by allowing
14:463:36074:15:14:93:524:170:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:it to be chosen optimally by the household in subperiod 1; but it is important that we still assume
14:464:36173:14:9:93:275:156:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:that it cannot be changed in subperiod 2.
14:465:36214:9:18:103:524:147:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:10One interpretation of the “cash-in-advance” constraint is that it actually represents a constraint
14:466:36314:18:0:93:524:129:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:on  the  type  of  assets  that  can  be  held  by  money-market  mutual  funds  (MMMFs).   But  such  a
15:467:36420:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central bank) or by bankers, are assumed equally to satisfy the constraint is intended
15:468:36506:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to  capture  the  way  in  which  the  demand  for  privately-issued  STSIs  is  observed  to
15:469:36599:17:17:93:510:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:vary with the supply of publicly-issued STSIs, as shown by Carlsonet al.(2014).
15:470:36678:17:18:111:525:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We do not, of course, deny that there arealsospecial uses for base money (currency
15:471:36760:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and reserve balances held at the Fed) as a means of payment, of the kind that Lucas
15:472:36843:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and Stokey sought to model.  In particular, when the supply of reserves by the Fed
15:473:36925:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is  sufficiently  restricted,  as  was  chronically  the  case  prior  to  the  financial  crisis  of
15:474:37026:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:2008,  the  special  convenience  of  reserve  balances  in  facilitating  payments  between
15:475:37118:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial intermediaries results in a spread between the yield on reserves and that on
15:476:37204:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:STSIs such as Treasury bills; and the control of this spread by varying the supply of
15:477:37289:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reserves was the focus of monetary policy prior to the crisis.  Nonetheless, the spread
15:478:37376:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:between the yield on reserves and the T-bill rate (or federal funds rate) is not the one
15:479:37464:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of interest to us here.  Under the circumstances in which the Fed has conducted its
15:480:37547:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:experiments with “quantitative easing,” the supply of reserves has been consistently
15:481:37631:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:well beyond the level needed to drive the T-bill yield down to (or even below) the
15:482:37713:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:yield on reserves.  Hence while certain kinds of payments by banks are constrained by
15:483:37798:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:their reserve balances, we may assume that this has not been a binding constraint in
15:484:37882:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the period in which we wish to consider the effects of further changes in the central-
15:485:37968:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank  balance  sheet.   And  granting  that  reserves  have  special  uses  that  can  result
15:486:38061:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in a liquidity premium specific to them (under circumstances no longer relevant at
15:487:38143:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:present) does not in any way imply that STSIs cannotalsohave special uses for which
15:488:38226:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:other assets will not serve, giving rise to another sort of money premium — one that
15:489:38310:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:need not be zero simply because the premium associated with reserve balances has
15:490:38390:17:17:93:177:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:been eliminated.
15:491:38406:17:18:111:525:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The acceptability of a financial claim as “cash” that can be used to purchase cash
15:492:38488:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods  is  assumed  to  depend  on  its  having  a  value  at  maturity  that  is  completely
15:493:38581:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:certain, rather than being state-contingent.  This requires not only that it be a claim
15:494:38668:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to  a  fixed  nominal  quantity  at  a  future  date,  but  that  it  be  viewed  as  completely
15:495:38764:18:21:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:safe,  for  one  of  two  possible  reasons:  either  it  is  a  liability  of  the  government  (or
15:496:38864:21:15:93:524:200:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:constraint gives rise to a “money premium” only to the extent that there are special advantages
15:497:38959:15:14:93:524:185:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:to investors of holding wealth in MMMFs;  the ability to move funds quickly from them to make
15:498:39052:14:14:93:524:171:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:purchases  is  one  such  advantage.   Rather  than  explicitly  introducing  a  demand  for  cash  on  the
15:499:39159:14:15:93:524:157:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:part of MMMFs and assuming that households use their MMMF balances to make certain types
15:500:39247:15:14:93:524:142:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of purchases, we obtain the same equilibrium money premium more simply by supposing that the
15:501:39339:14:0:93:416:128:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:STSIs can directly be used as a means of payment in certain transactions.
16:502:39414:0:18:93:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central bank),11or it is collateralized in a way that allows a holder of the claim to
16:503:39499:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be certain of realizing a definite nominal value from it.  We suppose that bankers can
16:504:39585:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:issue liabilities that will be accepted as cash, but that these liabilities will have to be
16:505:39676:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:backed by specific risky durables as collateral, and that the holder of the debt has the
16:506:39764:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:right to demand payment of the debt at any time, if they cease to remain confident
16:507:39846:17:17:93:434:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that the collateral will continue to guarantee the fixed value for it.
16:508:39916:17:18:111:525:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:When  bankers  purchase  risky  durables  in  the  first  subperiod,  they  can  finance
16:509:40004:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:some  portion  of  the  purchase  price  by  issuing  safe  debt  (that  can  be  used  by  the
16:510:40099:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:holder during the second sub-period to purchase cash goods),  collateralized by the
16:511:40182:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:durables that are acquired. If in the second subperiod, the “no-crisis” state is reached,
16:512:40271:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the  durables  can  continue  to  serve  as  collateral  for  safe  debt,  as  the  value  of  the
16:513:40369:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:asset in the third subperiod can in this case be anticipated with certainty.  In this
16:514:40454:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:case, bankers are able to roll over their short-term collateralized debt, and continue
16:515:40540:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to  hold  the  durables.   If  instead  the  “crisis”  state  is  reached,  the  durables  can  no
16:516:40638:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:longer collateralize safe debt, as there is now a positive probability that in the third
16:517:40726:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:subperiod the durables will be worthless.  In this case, holders of the safe debt demand
16:518:40814:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:repayment in the second sub-period, and the bankers must sell durables in a fire sale,
16:519:40900:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the amount required to pay off the short-term debt.  It is the right to force this
16:520:40985:17:18:93:491:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:liquidation that makes the debt issued by bankers in the first sub-period safe.
16:521:41064:18:17:111:525:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:To be more specific, we suppose that the sale of goods (and in particular, cash
16:522:41143:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods) occurs at the beginning of the second subperiod:  after it has been revealed
16:523:41226:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:whether the crisis state will occur, but before the decision whether to demand imme-
16:524:41310:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:diate repayment of the short-term debt is made.  Thus at the time that shoppers seek
16:525:41394:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to purchase cash goods,  they may hold liabilities issued by bankers that grant the
16:526:41477:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:holder the right to demand repayment at any time; it is the fact that the short-term
16:527:41561:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:debt  has  this  feature  that  allows  it  to  be  accepted  as  cash  in  the  market  for  cash
16:528:41659:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods.  After the market for cash goods has taken place, the holders of the bankers’
16:529:41743:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:short-term debt (who may now include the sellers of cash goods) decide whether to
16:530:41824:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand  immediate  repayment  of  the  debt.   At  this  point,  these  holders  (whether
16:531:41913:17:19:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shoppers  or  workers)  only  care  about  the  contribution  that  the  asset  will  make  to
16:532:42007:19:17:103:524:185:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:11Of  course,  a  claim on  a government  need not  be  completely  safe.  If,  however,  a  government
16:533:42110:17:15:93:524:168:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:borrows  in  its  own  fiat  currency,  and  if  it  is  committed  to  ensure  that  its  nominal  liabilities  are
16:534:42226:15:14:93:524:153:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:paid with certainty (by monetizing them if necessary), then it is possible for it to issue debt that is
16:535:42329:14:0:93:334:139:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:correctly viewed as completely safe (in nominal terms).
17:536:42386:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the  household’s  pooled  end-of-period  budget.   In  the  crisis  state,  they  will  choose
17:537:42480:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to demand repayment,  since this ensures them the face value of the debt,  whereas
17:538:42562:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:if they do not demand repayment, they will receive the face value of the debt with
17:539:42644:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:probabilityq <1,but will receive nothing if the “asset collapse” state occurs.  If they
17:540:42731:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand repayment, they receive a claim on the investors who purchase the collateral
17:541:42814:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the fire sale; such a claim is assumed to guarantee payment in the end-of-period
17:542:42897:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:settlement, if within the bound of the line of credit arranged for the investor in the
17:543:42983:18:17:93:171:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:first subperiod.
17:544:42999:17:17:111:525:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The  other  source  of  assets  that  count  as  cash  is  the  government.   Some  very
17:545:43087:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:short-term government liabilities (Treasury bills) count as cash.  In addition, we shall
17:546:43175:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:suppose that the central bank can issue liabilities that also count as cash. If the central
17:547:43266:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank increases its supply of SFSIs by purchasing Treasury bills (that are themselves
17:548:43350:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:SFSIs), the overall supply of cash will be unchanged.  (This is again a demonstration
17:549:43435:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that our concept of “cash” differs importantly from that of Lucas and Stokey.)  But if
17:550:43521:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the central bank purchases non-cash assets (either longer-term Treasury bonds, that
17:551:43604:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:are less able to facilitate transactions than are shorter-term bills,  or assets subject
17:552:43692:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to other kinds of risk) and finances these purchases by creating new short-term safe
17:553:43776:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:liabilities, it can increase the net supply of SFSIs.  We are interested in the effects of
17:554:43866:17:39:93:220:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this latter kind of policy.
17:555:43893:39:25:93:482:356:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:1.2    Budget Constraints and Definition of Equilibrium

21:692:54236:17:17:93:525:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tion of bothξtandηt(that is, whether a crisis occurs in periodt), that satisfies the

21:694:54407:19:18:103:524:259:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:18The assumption thatFtmust be paid whether or not the full line of credit is used is important
21:695:54502:18:14:93:524:241:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:because it prevents the household from simply asking for a large line of credit, as much as would be
21:696:54602:14:15:93:524:227:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:desired in the crisis state, and then not using all of it in the non-crisis state.  If that were possible
21:697:54707:15:14:93:524:212:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:at  no  cost,  the  non-state-contingency  of  the  credit  available  to  the  investor  would  have  no  bite.
21:698:54819:14:14:93:524:198:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:The assumption that the line of credit must be paid for whether used or not makes this costly, and
21:699:54917:14:15:93:524:184:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:results in the household’s wishingex postin the crisis state that it had provided more funds to the
21:700:55016:15:14:93:524:169:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:investor — though it also wishesex postin the non-crisis state that it had providedlesscredit to
21:701:55112:14:14:93:525:155:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f20:F:the investor.  This device implies that the credit available to the investor will be optimalon average,
21:702:55215:14:0:93:405:141:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:though not optimal in each state because it cannot be state-contingent.
22:703:55288:0:18:93:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:each possible history (ξt,ηt), given initial financial wealthA0and pre-existing invest-
22:704:55375:18:17:93:525:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ment goodsI−1,and given the state-contingent evolution of the prices, net transfers
22:705:55458:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from the government to households, and the borrowing limit.  An optimal plan is a
22:706:55539:17:18:93:270:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:feasible plan that maximizes (1.1).
22:707:55574:18:17:111:525:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Equilibrium requires that all markets for goods and assets clear.  Thus it requires
22:708:55657:17:29:93:287:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that in the first subperiod of periodt,

22:714:55907:17:17:93:524:479:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:held  by  the  central  bank).   Note  that  we  assume  for  simplicity  that  durables  fully
22:715:56002:17:18:93:524:462:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:depreciate after supplying a service flow (in the event that there is no asset collapse)

22:718:56256:17:18:93:524:410:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:B:F(It−1),and is independent of the quantityst−1of valuable durables in the previous
22:719:56338:18:17:93:129:392:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:period.
22:720:56345:17:29:111:483:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Equilibrium also requires that in the second subperiod, if a crisis occurs,
22:721:56420:29:29:282:525:346:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:A:s∗dt=s∗st,(1.14)
22:722:56436:29:30:93:366:317:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and that in either the crisis or in the non-crisis state,

22:726:56529:24:18:111:524:217:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f9:A:We can then define a (flexible-price) equilibrium as a specification of pricesQt,Γt
22:727:56612:18:17:93:524:199:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and yieldRmton cash for each historyξt,  and pricesPt, ̃Ptand bond yieldsRbtfor

23:732:57014:0:25:93:399:707:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:1.3    Fiscal Policy and Central-Bank Policy
23:733:57058:25:18:93:524:682:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:The equilibrium conditions above involve several variables that depend on government
23:734:57142:18:17:93:525:664:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policy:  the supplies of outside financial assets ̃MtandBst,the net transfersTt,and
23:735:57225:17:17:93:524:647:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the yieldsRmtandRbton the outside financial assets.  Fiscal policy determines the

23:740:57564:18:17:93:524:536:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:decide how much of existing claims on the government will be financed through STSIs
23:741:57647:17:17:93:524:519:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(issuance of Treasury bills), as opposed to longer-term debt that cannot be used to
23:742:57730:17:18:93:525:502:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:satisfy the cash-in-advance constraint.  If we let ̃Mgtbe T-bill issuance by the Treasury
23:743:57819:18:17:93:524:484:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the first subperiod of periodt, it follows that the total supply of longer-term debt
23:744:57906:17:29:93:235:467:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:by the Treasury will equal19
23:745:57934:29:30:251:525:438:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:A:Bgt=RmtLt−1− ̃Mgt.(1.18)
23:746:57958:30:17:111:525:408:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Of these longer-term securities issued by the Treasury, a quantityBcbtwill be held
23:747:58040:17:17:93:524:391:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:as assets of the central bank, backing central-bank liabilities ̃Mcbtof equal value.  We
23:748:58128:17:18:93:524:374:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shall suppose that all of these central-bank liabilities are STSIs that count as cash.
23:749:58214:18:26:93:431:356:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:The supply of outside assets to the private sector is then given by
23:750:58281:26:32:265:525:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A: ̃Mt≡ ̃Mgt+ ̃Mcbt,(1.19)
23:751:58305:32:24:264:525:298:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:A:Bst≡Bgt−Bcbt.(1.20)

23:753:58408:17:18:93:524:257:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of  periodtmust  equal  net  claimsLton  the  government.   (A  comparison  of  the
23:754:58491:18:17:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:definition ofWtin (1.8) with the definition ofLtin (1.17) shows that the market-

23:759:58836:18:0:93:265:138:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f17:F:have a market price of ( ̃Mgt+Bgt)/Rmt.
24:760:58877:0:27:93:296:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Since ̃Mcbt=Bcbt,we alternatively have
24:761:58915:27:26:266:525:680:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:A:At= ̃Mt+Bst,(1.21)
24:762:58933:26:17:93:411:654:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in terms of the supplies of outside assets to the private sector.
24:763:58998:17:18:111:525:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:At the end of periodt, the assets of the central bank are worth (Rbt/Rmt)Bcbt,while
24:764:59081:18:17:93:524:619:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:its liabilities are worth ̃Mcbt=Bcbt.In general, these quantities will not be equal; we
24:765:59168:17:17:93:524:602:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:suppose, however, that net balance-sheet earnings must be rebated to the Treasury
24:766:59249:17:27:93:357:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:at the end of the period, in a transfer of magnitude
24:767:59301:27:26:237:380:558:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:Tcbt=  (Rbt/Rmt)Bcbt− ̃Mcbt.
24:768:59329:26:17:93:524:532:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:A transfer from the central bank to the Treasury allows the Treasury to make a larger
24:769:59414:17:18:93:524:515:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:transfer to the private sector while achieving the same target for end-of-period claims
24:770:59501:18:17:93:524:497:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on the government.  However, this does not change formula (1.17) for the size of net
24:771:59585:17:17:93:524:480:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:transfer that is made to the private sector, because that equation was already written
24:772:59671:17:18:93:524:463:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in terms of a consolidated budget constraint for the Treasury and central bank.  If
24:773:59754:18:17:93:177:445:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:instead we write
24:774:59770:17:22:228:387:428:12:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f9:A:Tgt=Lt− ̃Mgt−(Rbt/Rmt)Bgt
24:775:59795:22:18:93:524:406:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for the net transfer from the Treasury required to achieve the targetLtneglecting
24:776:59876:18:26:93:304:388:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:any transfers from the central bank, then
24:777:59917:26:26:267:351:362:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:Tt=Tgt+Tcbt.
24:778:59929:26:18:111:525:336:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally,  in  addition  to  choosing  the  size  of  its  balance  sheet,  the  central  bank
24:779:60022:18:17:93:524:318:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can choose the nominal interest rateRmtpaid on its liabilities.  In our model, where
24:780:60106:17:17:93:524:301:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central-bank liabilities (reserves, reverse repos, or central-bank bills) are treated as
24:781:60194:17:18:93:524:284:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:perfect substitutes for all other forms of cash (Treasury bills or STSIs issued by private
24:782:60284:18:17:93:524:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:banks), this policy decision directly determines the equilibrium yield on those other
24:783:60369:17:17:93:524:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:forms of cash as well.20There are thus two independent dimensions of central-bank
24:784:60450:17:18:103:524:232:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:20In a more complex model in which reserve balances at the central bank play a special role that
24:785:60546:18:14:93:524:214:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:other STSIs cannot fulfill, and are in sufficiently scarce supply, there will be a spread between the
24:786:60647:14:15:93:524:200:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:interest rate paid on reserves and the equilibrium yield on other STSIs,  though the central bank
24:787:60744:15:14:93:524:185:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:will still have relatively direct control over the equilibrium yield on STSIs,  by varying either the
24:788:60845:14:14:93:524:171:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:interest rate paid on reserves or the degree of scarcity of reserves.  Even before the increased size
24:789:60946:14:15:93:524:157:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of central-bank balance sheets resulting from the financial crisis, many central banks implemented
24:790:61044:15:14:93:524:142:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:their interest-rate targets largely by varying the interest rate paid on reserve balances, as discussed
24:791:61147:14:0:93:220:128:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:in Woodford (2003, chap.  1).
25:792:61178:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policy each period, each of which can be chosen independently of fiscal policy (that
25:793:61262:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is,  of  the  evolution  of  both  total  claims  on  the  governmentLtand  the  supply  of
25:794:61353:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:short-term safe government liabilities), except to the extent that perhapsBcbtmust
25:795:61435:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be no greater thanBgt.21These can alternatively be described as implementation of
25:796:61516:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the central bank’s target for the interest rate paid on cash, and variation in the size
25:797:61603:17:17:93:424:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of its balance sheet holding fixed its target for that interest rate.
25:798:61672:17:18:111:525:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:There is a further potential dimension of central-bank policy, which is choice of
25:799:61753:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the composition of its balance sheet.  Above we have assumed that the central bank
25:800:61835:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:holds only longer-term Treasury securities, but it might also hold Treasury bills on
25:801:61919:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:its balance sheet (as indeed the Fed does).  In our model, however, it is easy to see
25:802:62004:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that  central-bank  acquisition  of  T-bills  (financed  by  issuing  central-bank  liabilities
25:803:62099:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that are perfect substitutes for T-bills and pay the same rate of interest) will have
25:804:62184:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:no effect on any other aspect of equilibrium.  To simplify the algebra, we do not even
25:805:62270:18:44:93:391:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:allow for this possibility in the notation introduced above.
25:806:62330:44:29:93:491:437:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:C:2    Determinants of Intertemporal Equilibrium
25:807:62376:29:17:93:524:408:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We turn now to a characterization of equilibrium in the model just described.  We
25:808:62457:17:18:93:524:391:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shall give particular attention to the determinants of the supply of and demand for
25:809:62540:18:17:93:524:373:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:safe assets, and the supply of and demand for risky durables, both when originally
25:810:62622:17:38:93:297:356:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:produced and in the event of a fire sale.
25:811:62663:38:25:93:362:318:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:2.1    Conditions for Optimal Behavior

25:814:62874:18:18:103:525:257:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:21In  fact,  within  the  logic  of  the  model,  there  is  no  problem  with  allowingBcbtto  exceedBgt;
25:815:62980:18:14:93:524:239:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:this would simply require negative holdings of government bonds by the private sector (issuance of
25:816:63078:14:14:93:524:225:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:“synthetic” bonds by the private sector),  which can already be accommodated in the constraints
25:817:63173:14:0:93:161:211:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:specified above.
26:818:63191:0:35:93:514:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:household (as defined in the previous section) is one that maximizes a Lagrangian

28:902:68752:22:14:93:524:373:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of existing durables at the end of each period, while the occurrence of an asset collapse affects the
28:903:68853:14:14:93:524:359:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:utility  of  the  household,  it  has  no  consequences  for  the  assets  carried  by  the  household  into  the

28:906:69159:14:15:93:524:316:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:occur in subperiod 3.  We assume that policy in periodst+ 1 and later is also independent of whether
28:907:69259:15:14:93:525:301:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:an asset collapse has occurred in periodt.  Given this, the relevant information set for equilibrium
28:908:69359:14:9:93:524:287:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:determination in subperiod 1 of periodt+1 is independent of whether an asset collapse has occurred.
28:909:69458:9:18:103:525:278:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f17:F:24Note thatRmt+1is the nominal yield between the settlement of accounts at the end of periodt
