29:921:70423:0:25:93:323:707:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:2.2    Characterizing Equilibrium
29:922:70456:25:18:93:524:682:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In an equilibrium, all of the necessary conditions for optimality of the household’s plan
29:923:70545:18:17:93:524:664:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:just listed must hold, and in addition, the market-clearing conditions (1.11)–(1.16)
29:924:70629:17:17:93:524:647:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:must hold.  We now draw some further conclusions about relations that must exist
29:925:70709:17:18:93:524:630:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:among  the  various  endogenous  variables  in  an  equilibrium,  in  order  to  understand
29:926:70800:18:17:93:323:612:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:how they are affected by central-bank policy.
29:927:70845:17:17:111:525:595:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:To simplify the discussion, in the present paper we shall restrict attention to the
29:928:70928:17:18:93:524:578:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:case in which any exogenous factors that change over time (apart from the occurrence
29:929:71012:18:17:93:524:560:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of crisis states and asset collapses, as depicted in Figure 1) are purely deterministic
29:930:71099:17:17:93:525:543:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(that  is,  simply  a  function  of  the  datet).   That  is,  when  we  consider  the  effects
29:931:71194:17:18:93:524:526:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of a temporary disturbance of any other type,  we shall consider only the case of a
29:932:71277:18:17:93:524:508:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shock that occurs in the initial periodt= 0,with consequences that are perfectly
29:933:71357:17:17:93:524:491:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:predictable  after  that.  We shall  also  restrict attention  to the  effects  of alternative
29:934:71451:17:18:93:524:474:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary and fiscal policies that are similarly deterministic;  this means that while
29:935:71536:18:17:93:524:456:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we can consider the effects of responding in different ways to a one-time disturbance
29:936:71621:17:17:93:524:439:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(in section xx below), we do not consider the effects of responding to the occurrence
29:937:71706:17:18:93:524:422:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of  a  crisis  that  results  in  a  fire  sale  of  bank  assets  (or  to  an  asset  collapse).   The
29:938:71809:18:17:93:524:404:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reason  is  that  our  concern  here  is  with  the  consequences  for  the  risks  to  financial
29:939:71906:17:17:93:525:387:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stability of alternative central-bank policiespriorto the occurrence of a crisis;  the
29:940:71992:17:18:93:524:370:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:interesting (but more complex) question of what can be achieved by suitable use of
29:941:72074:18:17:93:493:352:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:these instruments to respond to a crisisafterit occurs is left for a later study.
29:942:72155:17:17:111:525:335:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Under this assumption, neither the occurrence of a crisis nor an asset collapse in
29:943:72237:17:18:93:525:318:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:any periodtaffects equilibrium determination in subsequent periods, and we obtain
29:944:72318:18:17:93:525:300:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an equilibrium in which the variables listed above as functions of the historyξtdepend
29:945:72404:17:17:93:525:283:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:only on the datet, and those listed as functions of the history (ξt,ηt) will depend only
29:946:72492:17:18:93:524:266:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on the datetand the value ofηt.  Moreover, because the resolution of uncertainty
29:947:72572:18:17:93:524:248:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:during the period has no effect on equilibrium in later periods, the Lagrange multiplier
29:948:72660:17:17:93:524:231:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:B:φ6tindicating the shadow value of additional funds in the end-of-period settlement

43:1386:101756:45:26:93:524:517:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:F:3    The Size of the Central-Bank Balance Sheet and
43:1387:101807:26:29:122:318:491:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:C:Stationary Equilibrium
43:1388:101829:29:18:93:524:462:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We wish to compare the effects of the two dimensions of central-bank policy:  vari-
43:1389:101912:18:17:93:525:444:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ation  in  its  target  for  the  interest  rateRmtpaid  on  cash,  and  variation  in  the  size
43:1390:102009:17:17:93:524:427:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of its balance sheet holding fixed its target for that interest rate.  We first compare
43:1391:102096:17:18:93:524:410:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:alternative  possible  long-run  stationary  equilibria,  in  which  the  inflation  rate,  the
43:1392:102191:18:17:93:524:392:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:various interest rates, and relative prices are all constant over time, and the real size
43:1393:102280:17:17:93:524:375:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the central-bank balance sheet and the real supply of T-bills by the Treasury are
43:1394:102364:17:18:93:524:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constant over time as well.  We can show that there exists a two-dimensional family of
43:1395:102450:18:17:93:524:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:such stationary equilibria.  Moreover, fixing the real supply of Treasury bills, it is still
43:1396:102542:17:17:93:524:323:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:possible to move in both directions within this two-dimensional family of stationary
43:1397:102626:17:18:93:524:306:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibria by varying the two independent dimensions of central-bank policy.  Thus
43:1398:102708:18:17:93:524:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:even a simple consideration of stationary equilibria allows us to observe the separate
43:1399:102794:17:38:93:290:271:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effects of the two dimensions of policy.

45:1460:106565:17:18:93:525:358:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:must have a unique solution forλ.The associated stationary level of cash balances can
45:1461:106650:18:17:93:524:340:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be any level greater than or equal tom∗≡c∗1(λ).Hence such a stationary equilibrium
45:1462:106732:17:17:93:459:323:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:exists in the case of any value of   ̃mthat is greater than or equal tom∗.
45:1463:106806:17:18:111:525:306:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, in any stationary equilibrium, the equilibrium real return on longer-term
45:1464:106888:18:17:93:524:288:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bonds (and indeed, any asset that can neither be used as cash nor used as collateral
45:1465:106972:17:28:93:413:271:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in order to issue liabilities that can be used as cash) will equal
45:1466:107038:28:28:232:386:243:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:E[Rb]/Π  =Rm ̃φ1/Π  =β−1.
45:1467:107063:28:18:93:524:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Note that this is independent of both   ̃mand Π.  Thus a higher value ofRm/Π   =
45:1468:107143:18:17:93:524:197:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:1 +rm(  ̃m) corresponds to a reduced spread between the returns on longer-term bonds
45:1469:107227:17:17:93:525:180:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and those on holding cash.  We also note that the value of  ̃φ1(or more precisely, the
45:1470:107313:17:18:93:256:163:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:log of  ̃φ1) measures this spread.
45:1471:107347:18:17:111:525:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We thus find that there is a two-dimensional family of possible stationary equilib-
45:1472:107430:17:0:93:524:128:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ria, which can be indexed by the choice of the two policy variables Π and   ̃m, which
46:1473:107517:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can be independently varied using the two dimensions of central-bank policy: conven-
46:1474:107601:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tional monetary policy (interest-rate policy) and balance-sheet policy (quantitative
46:1475:107685:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing).   These  two  dimensions  of  monetary  policy  have  quite  different  effects.   In
46:1476:107779:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:our flexible-price model, interest-rate policy has no effect on any real variables, but
46:1477:107866:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can be used (within the limit imposed by the zero lower bound) to control inflation.
46:1478:107950:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Balance-sheet policy (changing the total supply of outside safe assets by increasing
46:1479:108034:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:or reducing the quantity of longer-term bonds held by the central bank) can instead
46:1480:108117:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:affect  the  steady-state  values  of  all  of  the  real  variables  in  our  model,  except  that
46:1481:108216:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f10:B:further increases in the real supply of outside safe assets beyond the level   ̃m=m∗
46:1482:108300:17:18:93:210:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:have no further effects.
46:1483:108324:18:17:111:525:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The possible stationary values of the various real variables that can be achieved
46:1484:108405:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by alternative monetary policies can thus be fully characterized by considering the
46:1485:108488:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:one-parameter family of stationary equilibria corresponding to different values of   ̃m.
46:1486:108576:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:These equilibria can be classified as of three possible types, according to which of the
46:1487:108664:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial constraints bind.  (The three possible cases correspond to the three cases
46:1488:108748:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:discussed in our treatment in the previous section of the endogenous determination
46:1489:108830:18:17:93:219:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the safe asset supply.)
46:1490:108856:17:17:111:525:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:First, there are equilibria in which the real outside supply of safe assets equals or
46:1491:108941:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:exceeds the levelm∗required for satiation;  in these equilibria,  the cash-in-advance
46:1492:109026:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraint  is  slack,  bankers  finance  none  of  their  purchases  of  durables  by  issuing
46:1493:109121:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:collateralized short-term debt (so that the collateral constraint on such issuance is
46:1494:109206:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:also slack), and as no assets are sold in a fire sale even if the crisis state occurs, there
46:1495:109298:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is no ex post regret of the size of investors’ credit limit (so that the constraint that
46:1496:109386:17:17:93:349:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this must be fixed in advance also does not bind).
46:1497:109436:17:18:111:525:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Second,  there  are  equilibria  in  which  the  real  outside  supply  of  safe  assets  is
46:1498:109528:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:insufficient, and there is some private issuance of safe debt, but the quantity of safe
46:1499:109615:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:debt issued by bankers is still small enough for the collateral constraint not to bind.
46:1500:109702:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:And  third,  there  are  equilibria  in  which  the  incentive  for  issuance  of  safe  debt  by
46:1501:109799:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bankers is so strong that their issuance of such liabilities is limited by the availability
46:1502:109890:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of suitable collateral.  The three cases correspond to different ranges of real outside
46:1503:109977:17:18:93:525:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:supply of safe assets:  high values of   ̃m, an intermediate range of values of   ̃m,and low

49:1602:115339:17:17:93:524:161:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:value, the equilibrium production of durables now increases more rapidly with further
49:1603:115424:17:0:93:198:144:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:reductions inRm/Π.
50:1604:115444:0:18:111:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 3 shows the stationary values of another set of variables, across the same
50:1605:115525:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:one-parameter family of stationary equilibria:  the supply of short-term collateralized
50:1606:115612:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:debt ̃D(the stationary value of the variable ̃Dt≡ ̃φ6tDt), the resulting total supply
50:1607:115697:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of cashˆM,the upper bound ̃Γson issuance of short-term debt by bankers given by
50:1608:115776:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the expected market value of their assets in the event of a crisis,  and for purposes
50:1609:115861:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of comparison, the market value ̃Qsof those same assets in subperiod 1.37One sees
50:1610:115942:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that as the equilibrium return on cash falls, and the money premium correspondingly
50:1611:116025:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increases,  as one moves from the right boundary of the figure to the left,  that the
50:1612:116110:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:issuance of short-term debt by banks increases from an initial value of zero (when
50:1613:116192:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the money premium is zero) to progressively higher values.  The rate of increase is
50:1614:116275:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sharpest in the high-cash-return region, because the upper bound on debt issuance
50:1615:116356:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:does not bind; after that constraint begins to bind (aroundRm/Π = 0.91), ̃Dincreases
50:1616:116440:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:less  sharply  with  further  declines  inRm/Π,as  it  can  only  increase  to  the  extent
50:1617:116531:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that ̃Γsalso increases.  In fact,  in the high-cash-return region, ̃Γsdecreases as the
50:1618:116617:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:money premium increases; the reason is that, as short-term debt issuance increases
50:1619:116699:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the quantity of assets that must be sold in a fire sale in the event of a crisis increases,
50:1620:116790:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:depressing  the  fire-sale  value  of  bankers’  assets.   OnceRm/Π  falls  to  around  0.91,
50:1621:116883:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the constraint comes to bind, both because of the increase in desired debt issuance
50:1622:116966:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f2:B:andthe reduction in the value of the collateral available to back such debt.  Beyond
50:1623:117050:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this point, further increases in the size of the money premium cause ̃Γsto increase,
50:1624:117134:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rather than continuing to decrease; this is because the value of relaxing the constraint
50:1625:117222:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on short-term debt issuance now contributes to a larger market value of durables in
50:1626:117305:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:subperiod 1,38which induces a larger market supply of durables (as can be seen from
50:1627:117388:17:14:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:theIcurve in Figure 2), so that ̃Γsincreases slightly, even though the fire-sale price
50:1628:117474:14:19:94:189:294:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B: ̃Γ continues to fall.
50:1629:117496:19:18:103:524:275:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:37Each of these variables is measured in marginal-utility units, as they have a constant value in
50:1630:117593:18:14:93:524:257:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:marginal-utility units in a stationary equilibrium, regardless of the rate of inflation.  Also, we have
50:1631:117696:14:15:93:524:243:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:shown above that the equilibrium relations determining the values of these variables are in many
50:1632:117792:15:9:93:475:228:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:cases simpler when written in terms of the variables expressed in marginal-utility units.
50:1633:117881:9:18:103:524:219:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:38Specifically, the value of  ̃φ1 ̃Q/λincreases, which is the ratio of the marginal-utility value of the
50:1634:117985:18:15:93:524:201:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:sale price of a unit of the durable good in subperiod 1, given that payment received in subperiod 1
50:1635:118084:15:14:93:524:186:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:can be used to acquire cash for use by the shopper, to the marginal-utility value of the sale price
50:1636:118183:14:14:93:524:172:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:of a unit of normal goods in subperiod 2.  This relative price determines the incentive to produce
50:1637:118281:14:15:93:524:158:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:additional investment goods, as shown by condition (2.12), and hence the supply of durables.  Note
50:1638:118379:15:0:93:515:143:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:that the stationary value of ̃Qdoesnotincrease, as can be seen from the ̃Qscurve in this figure.
51:1639:118477:0:18:111:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We can also see, from the size of the gap between the solid line indicating the value
51:1640:118562:18:17:93:525:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ofˆMand the dashed line indicating the value of ̃D, how the part of the cash supply
51:1641:118645:17:17:93:525:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that comes from outside safe assets (the value ofλ ̃m, in marginal-utility units) varies
51:1642:118733:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:across the alternative stationary equilibria. This value decreases monotonically as one
51:1643:118820:18:17:93:523:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:proceeds from right to left in the figure, both because ̃Dincreases and becauseˆM
51:1644:118901:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:decreases; the latter effect represents the reduction in the demand for cash balances
51:1645:118986:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:as the opportunity cost of holding them (i.e.,  the money premium) increases.  The
51:1646:119068:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:fact that the equilibrium relationship between the size of the money premium and the
51:1647:119152:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:quantity of outside safe assets is monotonic indicates how the choice of a stationary
51:1648:119237:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:level for the supply of outside safe assets (through the combination of the Treasury’s
51:1649:119323:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:debt-management policy and the central bank’s balance-sheet policy) can be used to
51:1650:119405:17:17:93:525:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:determine the stationary value ofRm/Π, and thus to select which of the stationary
51:1651:119486:17:18:93:340:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibria depicted in these figures should occur.
51:1652:119536:18:17:111:525:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Note that there is a limit to how farRm/Π can be reduced by shrinking the supply
51:1653:119616:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of outside safe assets; at the left edge of the figure,   ̃mfalls to zero, whileRm/Π is still
51:1654:119709:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:positive.  (This is because this lower bound does not correspond to an opportunity
51:1655:119791:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cost high enough to reduce the demand for cash balances to zero; it is only necessary
51:1656:119876:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that the demand for cash balances fall to a low enough level that it is no greater than
51:1657:119963:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the quantity of safe  liabilities that bankers wish  to supply,  which grows the larger
51:1658:120050:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the money premium gets.)  However, this lower bound forRm/Π can easily be well
51:1659:120128:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:below 1 (as shown in the figure), corresponding to a negative long-run equilibrium
51:1660:120210:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:short-term real rate.  Thus our model is one in which it is perfectly possible to have
51:1661:120296:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an  equilibrium  short-term  real  rate  that  remains  negative  forever,  as  a  result  of  a
51:1662:120392:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shortage of safe assets; this results in a “safety trap” in the sense of Caballero and
51:1663:120478:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Farhi  (2013),  in  the  case  that  the  inflation  target  Π  is  too  low.   An  advantage  of
51:1664:120575:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:working with a fully developed monetary equilibrium model, however, is that we see
51:1665:120657:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that the existence of a safety trap depends not simply on too low a supply of safe
51:1666:120739:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets (or too great a demand for them), butalsoon choosing too low an inflation
51:1667:120819:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:target, just as in the “liquidity trap” model of Krugman (1998) and Eggertsson and
51:1668:120901:17:17:93:183:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Woodford (2003).

53:1721:124191:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(normalized) Lagrange multipliers in our model:   ̃φ1(which indicates a binding cash-

53:1732:125101:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:starting from zero distortion whenRm/Π =β−1,so that there is no money premium.
53:1733:125179:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Moreover,  the  magnitude  of  the  distortion  is  a  convex  function  of  the  size  of  the
53:1734:125274:18:18:93:524:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:money premium, so that the rate at which the distortion increases becomes greater
53:1735:125355:18:17:103:524:151:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:40Note that the quantity  ̃φ1−1 plotted in the figure is also the value of  ̃φ4,as well as 1−ptimes

54:1752:125532:252:17:93:524:405:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Figure 5:  Lagrange multipliers indicating the degree to which the various financial
54:1753:125616:17:17:93:524:388:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraints bind, in alternative stationary equilibria corresponding to different con-
54:1754:125702:17:35:93:206:371:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:stant values ofRm/Π.
54:1755:125722:35:17:93:299:336:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for larger values of the money premium.

54:1757:125843:18:17:93:525:301:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monotonic functions of   ̃φc5(the first an increasing function,  the latter a decreasing

54:1761:126199:17:17:93:524:232:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(in both states) owing to the possibility of a fire sale of assets by banks.  The figure
54:1762:126287:17:18:93:525:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shows that the magnitude of this distortion also increases asRm/Π is reduced, starting

54:1765:126532:18:17:93:524:162:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cash-return  region;  once  the  availability  of  collateral  becomes  a  binding  constraint
54:1766:126626:17:0:93:524:145:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on issuance of short-term debt by bankers, the degree of inefficiency in the level of
55:1767:126713:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:production of special goods increases only gradually with further increases in the size
55:1768:126800:18:17:93:213:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the money premium.
55:1769:126821:17:17:111:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, the figure indicates that  ̃φ3>0,indicating that the constraint that short-
55:1770:126905:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:term debt issuance cannot exceed the amount that can be backed by the collateral
55:1771:126985:18:17:93:525:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:value of bankers’ assets binds,  only for values ofRm/Π less than 0.91.  Below this
55:1772:127068:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:point, however, the value of the multiplier rises sharply with further increases in the
55:1773:127155:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:money premium;  this accounts for the increase in the subperiod 1 market price of
55:1774:127236:18:38:93:354:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:durables, shown in Figure 4, over this same region.
55:1775:127287:38:25:93:515:547:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:3.2    Consequences of a Larger Central-Bank Balance Sheet
55:1776:127345:25:17:93:524:522:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We  can  now  consider  how  a  quantitative  easing  policy  that  permanently  increases
55:1777:127435:17:18:93:524:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the size of the central bank’s balance sheet (in real terms, or relative to the size of
55:1778:127522:18:17:93:524:487:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the economy) — and more specifically, a policy of purchasing longer-term assets and
55:1779:127605:17:17:93:524:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financing these purchases by issuing short-term safe liabilities — affects the economy’s
55:1780:127693:17:18:93:524:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:long-run equilibrium.  To the extent that the effects of the policy are not undercut by
55:1781:127780:18:17:93:524:435:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f3:B:an offsetting shift in the maturity composition of the debt issued by the Treasury,41
55:1782:127865:17:17:93:525:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:such a policy can increase the steady-state level of   ̃m.If   ̃m < m∗,so that there is
55:1783:127952:17:18:93:524:401:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:not already satiation of the demand for safe assets even without any creation of safe
55:1784:128037:18:17:93:524:383:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets  by  the  private  sector,  then  increasing   ̃mwill  mean  moving  to  a  stationary
55:1785:128130:17:17:93:524:366:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium with a higher value ofRm/Π,corresponding to a movement further to
55:1786:128207:17:18:93:327:349:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the right in each of the figures just presented.
55:1787:128255:18:17:111:525:331:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:This  has  real  effects,  and  in  particular  has  consequences  for  financial  stability.
55:1788:128348:17:17:93:524:314:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:However, a larger supply of outside safe assets as a result of a policy of quantitative
55:1789:128435:17:18:93:525:297:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing shouldimprovefinancial stability.  Specifically, whether the economy begins in
55:1790:128520:18:17:93:525:279:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the low-cash-return or high-cash-return region, a higher value ofRm/Π (and hence
55:1791:128600:17:17:93:524:262:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a  smaller  money  premium)  reduces  private  issuance  of  short-term  debt ̃D.   As  a
55:1792:128689:17:18:93:525:245:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:consequence, it reduces the quantitys∗of durables that will have to be sold in a fire
55:1793:128774:18:17:93:524:227:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sale in the event of a crisis, and so reduces the severity of the distortions associated
55:1794:128862:17:18:93:525:210:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:with a crisis.42Both the degree to which durables are under-valued in the crisis (as
55:1795:128946:18:18:103:524:192:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:41Note that such a shift in Treasury policy did offset a significant part of the effect of the Fed’s
55:1796:129046:18:10:93:397:174:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:asset purchases in recent years, as shown by Greenwoodet al.(2014).
55:1797:129113:10:17:103:524:164:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:42Note that in the simple model presented here, theprobabilityof a crisis is exogenous, and so
55:1798:129207:17:15:93:524:147:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:cannot be affected by policy.  But policy can affect the severity of a crisis, conditional on the crisis
55:1799:129311:15:0:93:180:132:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:state being reached.
56:1800:129333:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:shown in Figure 4) and the degree of inefficiency in the level of production of special
56:1801:129420:18:17:93:460:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:goods (as shown in Figure 2) are smaller, the larger the value ofRm/Π.
56:1802:129490:17:17:111:525:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Thus from the standpoint of financial stability, a larger central-bank balance sheet
56:1803:129574:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is clearly to be preferred (at least as far as long-run steady states are concerned).  In
56:1804:129663:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:fact,  the  other  real  effects  of  a  quantitative  easing  policy  on  the  long-run  steady
56:1805:129759:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:state are also beneficial.  A higher value ofRm/Π implies that the cash-in-advance
56:1806:129841:17:18:93:525:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:constraint  binds  less  tightly  (as  shown  by  the  value  of   ̃φ1in  Figure  5),  and  this
56:1807:129937:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:results  in  a  more  efficient  allocation  of  household  expenditure  on  cash  and  credit
56:1808:130031:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods between the two types of goods (a ratio ofc1/c2closer to 1, in Figure 2).  And
56:1809:130115:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in the low-cash-return region (where  ̃φ3>0), a higher value ofRm/Π also results in
56:1810:130198:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:less over-valuation of durables in subperiod 1,  so that there is less inefficient over-
56:1811:130286:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:production of durables (as is also seen in Figure 2).  Thus each of these considerations
56:1812:130374:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:points in the same direction:  the equilibrium allocation of resources is more efficient
56:1813:130462:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(and  the  welfare  of  the  representative  household  is  increased)  if  the  real  supply  of
56:1814:130559:17:17:93:252:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:outside safe assets is increased.
56:1815:130592:17:18:111:525:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The conclusion that expansion of the central bank’s balance sheet is associated
56:1816:130671:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:with  a  more  efficient  allocation  of  resources  between  cash  and  credit  goods  might
56:1817:130764:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:seem surprising in light of the analysis of Lucas and Stokey (1987),  who conclude,
56:1818:130847:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in  the  context  of  a  similar  model  (but  without  durable  goods  production  or  fire
56:1819:130939:18:17:93:525:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sales),  that  efficiency  in  this  respect  is  greater  thelower  the  rate  of  growthof  the
56:1820:131036:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary base — with the highest levels of efficiency (and hence of welfare for the
56:1821:131119:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:representative  household)  being  achieved  only  in  the  case  of  steady  contraction  of
56:1822:131212:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the  size  of  the  central  bank’s  balance  sheet.   The  difference  in  conclusions  results
56:1823:131308:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from their assumption that the safe liabilities that count as cash must earn a nominal
56:1824:131394:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:interest rate of zero (so thatRm= 1 is assumed).  In that case, steady states with
56:1825:131476:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:different values ofRm/Π must correspond to different rates of inflation Π — whereas
56:1826:131559:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:here the choice of the inflation target Π is independent of the aspects of policy that
56:1827:131645:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:determineRm/Π, within the bound required by the lower bound on nominal interest
56:1828:131724:18:17:93:121:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:rates.
56:1829:131730:17:17:111:525:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Lucas and Stokey conclude, as we do, that relaxation of the cash-in-advance con-
56:1830:131810:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:straint, and a more efficient allocation of expenditure between cash and credit goods,
56:1831:131896:18:17:93:525:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:requires a higher value ofRm/Π,but in their analysis this requires a lower rate of
56:1832:131978:17:14:93:524:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:inflation, and hence a lower rate of growth of thenominalvalue of outside safe assets
56:1833:132063:14:0:97:525:138:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B: ̃Mt.In our model, it is also true that in a long-run stationary equilibrium, the rate of
57:1834:132154:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:growth of ̃Mtmust equal the inflation rate.  But it is possible for the central bank to
57:1835:132241:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f9:B:control the value of the currency unit other than through its control of the path of ̃Mt
57:1836:132329:17:14:93:525:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:(by appropriate variation inRmt), so that there is a decision to make about how large
57:1837:132414:14:21:97:525:658:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B: ̃Mtshould be relative to the level ofPtaimed at through interest-rate policy, that is
57:1838:132500:21:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:separate from the question of the long-run rate of growth of both variables.  Thus it
57:1839:132585:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is not correct, more generally, to identify a decision to increase the size of the cen-
57:1840:132672:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tral bank’s balance sheet with a decision to pursue a moreinflationarypolicy; in the
57:1841:132756:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:long run, these are two distinct issues.  The short-run consequences of balance-sheet
57:1842:132841:17:44:93:326:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:expansion are instead considered in section 5.
57:1843:132887:44:27:93:524:524:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:F:4    Quantitative Easing Compared with Macropru-
57:1844:132935:27:29:122:238:497:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:C:dential Policy
57:1845:132949:29:17:93:524:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Another implication of increasing the supply of central-bank reserves through a quan-
57:1846:133034:17:17:93:524:451:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:titative easing policy,  not discussed in the analysis above,  is relaxation of the con-
57:1847:133122:17:18:93:524:434:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:straint on private banks’ ability to issue money-like liabilities that may result from a
57:1848:133210:18:17:93:524:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:requirement that they hold reserves in proportion to their issuance of such liabilities.
57:1849:133298:17:17:93:524:399:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:Such reserve requirements apply (at least in some countries, like the US) to at least
57:1850:133383:17:18:93:524:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:some  kinds  of  short-term  safe  instruments  issued  by  commercial  banks  —  though
57:1851:133471:18:17:93:524:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:not, even in the US, to the kind of privately issued STSIs that were most responsible
57:1852:133556:17:17:93:525:347:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for the financial fragility exposed by the recent crisis.43And under many traditional
57:1853:133641:17:18:93:524:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:textbook accounts of the way that monetary policy affects the economy, the key ef-
57:1854:133723:18:17:93:524:312:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:fect of a central-bank open-market operation is precisely to relax this constraint on
57:1855:133808:17:17:93:524:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:private  bank  behavior  by  increasing  the  quantity  of  reserves  that  are  available  to
57:1856:133902:17:18:93:524:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:satisfy the reserve requirement.  This might seem to have important implications for
57:1857:133986:18:17:93:524:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability that would cut in the opposite direction to the analysis above; that
57:1858:134074:17:17:93:524:243:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is, it might seem that expansion of the central bank’s balance sheet should have as
57:1859:134157:17:18:93:524:226:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:an  effect,  or  even  as  its  primary  effect,  an  increase  in  the  extent  to  which  private
57:1860:134256:18:18:93:524:208:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:banks acquire risky assets and finance those assets by issuing money-like liabilities.
57:1861:134342:18:18:103:524:190:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:43The kinds of liabilities, such as retail deposits at commercial banks, to which such requirements
57:1862:134441:18:14:93:524:172:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:apply were not the ones the demand for which proved to highly volatile.  While these funds could in
57:1863:134540:14:14:93:524:158:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:principle be withdrawn on short notice, they were not, probably owing to the existence of deposit
57:1864:134637:14:0:93:428:144:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:insurance; and so they were not responsible for any appreciable funding risk.
58:1865:134716:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:This  is  in  fact  a  key  theme  of  the  analysis  by  Stein  (2012),  and  the  basis  for  the
58:1866:134815:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:proposal there that monetary policy decisions be considered from the standpoint of
58:1867:134897:17:17:93:252:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:“financial-stability regulation.”
58:1868:134930:17:18:111:525:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In  the  analysis  here,  we  have  abstracted  from  reserve  requirements,  since  even
58:1869:135019:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in  the  US,  these  have  not  been  binding  constraints  on  banks’  behavior  during  the
58:1870:135112:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:period  when  the  Fed’s  experiments  with  quantitative  easing  have  occurred.44We
58:1871:135198:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:can,  however,  use our framework to discuss the consequences for financial stability
58:1872:135283:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of increasing or decreasing the cost to financial institutions of issuing collateralized
58:1873:135371:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:short-term  debt  as  a  source  of  financing,  even  when  they  hold  sufficient  assets  to
58:1874:135466:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:provide the collateral for such issuance.  But we view this as a separate dimension of
58:1875:135552:18:17:93:525:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policy —macroprudentialpolicy — that should be distinguished, conceptually, from
58:1876:135632:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:both conventional monetary policy (interest-rate policy) and central-bank balance-
58:1877:135714:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sheet policy.45One might well use instruments of macroprudential policy that affect
58:1878:135797:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the ability and/or incentives of banks to issue money-like liabilities that are unrelated
58:1879:135886:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to the central bank’s balance sheet (and that do not depend on the existence of reserve
58:1880:135973:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:requirements).  And even when the tool that is used is a reserve requirement, one can
58:1881:136058:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:loosen or tighten this constraint independently of the way one that changes the size
58:1882:136142:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of the central bank’s balance sheet; first, because one can vary the required reserve
58:1883:136227:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ratio as well as the supply of reserves, and second, because the central bank can vary
58:1884:136313:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the supply of STSIs without varying the supply of reserves, if it issues central-bank
58:1885:136398:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bills or engages in reverse repo transactions,46or by varying the quantity of Treasury
58:1886:136484:17:18:93:246:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bills on its own balance sheet.
58:1887:136515:18:17:111:525:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The effects of varying macroprudential policy are in fact quite different from the
58:1888:136597:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effects (considered above) of varying the central bank’s supply of outside safe assets,
58:1889:136684:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:when the latter policy is implemented in a way that has no direct effects on finan-
58:1890:136767:18:18:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cial institutions’ cost of short-term debt issuance.  We can introduce macroprudential
58:1891:136853:18:17:103:524:255:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:44They were not relevant, even earlier, for most of the kinds of financing decisions modeled in this
58:1892:136953:17:15:93:524:238:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:paper.  As noted earlier, the privately supplied “cash” in this model should be identified primarily
58:1893:137053:15:9:93:292:223:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:with repos or asset-backed commercial paper.
58:1894:137097:9:18:103:524:214:7:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f5:F:45Macroprudential  policy,  modeled  in  a  way  similar  to  that  used  here,  is  also  compared  with
58:1895:137202:18:14:93:524:196:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:conventional monetary policy in Sergeyev (2016), which also discusses Ramsey policy when the two

58:1897:137396:15:9:93:446:167:10:g_d0_f5:10:g_d0_f5:F:treat the use of balance-sheet policies of the kind that are the central focus here.

65:2103:150076:44:26:93:524:541:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:F:5    Conventional   and   Unconventional   Monetary
65:2104:150127:26:29:122:499:515:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:C:Policy in the Presence of Nominal Rigidities
65:2105:150171:29:18:93:524:486:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:In the analysis thus far,  all prices have been assumed to be perfectly flexible,  and
65:2106:150257:18:17:93:524:468:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to  clear  markets  each  period.   In  such  a  model,  conventional  monetary  policy  has
65:2107:150349:17:17:93:524:451:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:no real effects, and affects only the general level of prices in terms of the monetary
65:2108:150435:17:18:93:524:434:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:unit.  It follows that conventional monetary policy has no consequences for financial
65:2109:150520:18:17:93:524:416:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stability.   This  establishes  a  sharp  distinction  between  the  effects  of  conventional
65:2110:150614:17:17:93:524:399:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy (interest-rate policy) and balance-sheet policy, since as shown above,
65:2111:150700:17:18:93:524:382:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the  central  bank’s  balance  sheet  (specifically,  therealsupply  of  safe  assets  by  the
65:2112:150794:18:17:93:398:364:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:central bank) does have consequences for financial stability.
65:2113:150855:17:17:111:525:347:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Such an analysis is adequate for consideration of the possible long-run stationary
65:2114:150937:17:18:93:524:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:equilibria achievable under alternative policies, as in the previous two sections.  But it
65:2115:151027:18:17:93:524:312:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:does not suffice for an analysis of the considerations at play when alternative dimen-
65:2116:151113:17:17:93:524:295:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:sions of monetary policy are used to address short-run macroeconomic stabilization
65:2117:151195:17:18:93:524:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:objectives, and this is the context in which central banks’ recent experiments with
65:2118:151278:18:17:93:524:260:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:quantitative easing have been conducted.  To address the issues raised by recent poli-
65:2119:151364:17:17:93:524:243:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cies, we need to consider the consequences for financial stability of using quantitative
65:2120:151452:17:18:93:524:226:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing as a substitute for an interest-rate cut that is prevented by the effective lower
65:2121:151540:18:17:93:524:208:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bound on short-term nominal interest rates, in a situation where such an interest-rate
65:2122:151626:17:17:93:477:191:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:cut would otherwise be desired in order to achieve a higher level of output.
65:2123:151702:17:18:111:525:174:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The  notion  that  an  interest-rate  cut  would  be  desired  in  order  to  increase  real
65:2124:151794:18:17:93:524:156:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:activity only makes sense in the presence of nominal rigidities of some kind.  Here
65:2125:151877:17:0:93:524:139:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we discuss a simple extension of the model presented above, that shows how sticky
66:2126:151960:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:prices allow conventional monetary policy to have real effects in the short run, while
66:2127:152046:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:it affects only the general level of prices in the long run.  We can then compare the
66:2128:152131:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effects  of quantitative  easing to  those  of an  interest-rate  cut,  both  with  respect  to
66:2129:152226:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the effects of these policies on aggregate demand, and their consequences for financial
66:2130:152313:18:38:93:137:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stability.
66:2131:152323:38:25:93:488:599:14:g_d0_f7:14:g_d0_f7:C:5.1    Equilibrium with a Sticky Price for Normal Goods
66:2132:152378:25:17:93:525:574:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We suppose that it is only the pricePtof normal goods that must be set in advance,
66:2133:152460:17:18:93:524:557:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:while the prices of special goods, durable goods, and all financial assets are assumed to
66:2134:152549:18:17:93:524:539:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be perfectly flexible, as above.  (Because all three types of normal goods are perfect
66:2135:152635:17:17:93:524:522:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:substitutes  from  the  standpoint  of  their  suppliers,  we  suppose  that  a  single  price
66:2136:152729:17:18:93:524:505:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f2:B:Ptis  posted,  at  which  goods  of  any  of  these  types  can  be  purchased;  we  suppose
66:2137:152821:18:17:93:524:487:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that  the  buyer  determines  which  type  of  good  will  be  obtained.)   For  simplicity,
66:2138:152913:17:17:93:524:470:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we  also  consider  here  the  case  of  a  single  unexpected  aggregate  shock  (apart  from
66:2139:153007:17:18:93:524:453:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the kind of uncertainty represented in Figure 1) at some datet, in response to which
66:2140:153091:18:17:93:524:435:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy (both interest-rate policy and balance-sheet policy) may be adjusted;
66:2141:153176:17:17:93:524:418:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:we suppose that there is no further uncertainty (except for the kind depicted in Figure
66:2142:153263:17:18:93:524:401:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:1) about how the economy will evolve after this shock occurs, and that the shock is
66:2143:153346:18:17:93:342:383:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:completely unanticipated prior to its occurrence.
66:2144:153395:17:17:111:525:366:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The  fact  that  the  shock  is  completely  unexpected  means  that  before  it  occurs,

76:2452:173770:17:18:93:524:336:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:on the money premium and equilibrium investment in risky real assets (upper graph)

76:2456:174084:17:18:93:524:249:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:similar to those of an interest-rate cut:  financial conditions are eased, the aggregate
76:2457:174172:18:17:93:524:231:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand for normal goods increases (both because of an increase in the demand for

76:2460:174419:18:17:93:524:179:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:issuance by banks, leading to larger expected distortions in the case that a crisis state
76:2461:174508:17:17:93:207:162:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f8:B:occurs in periodt+ 1.

77:2466:174875:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by a greater amount.54This can be seen from the fact that (5.4) must apply in either

77:2471:175302:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:in aggregate demand comes from increased demand for credit goods, as opposed to

78:2523:178987:17:17:93:524:232:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effects of the quantitative easing on desired investment demand, so that there is no
78:2524:179071:17:18:93:524:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:net change inIt.  Since the former policy change will reduceλtmore than the latter

78:2526:179240:17:17:93:524:180:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:and an increase in the demand for credit goods.  Since there is (by hypothesis) no
78:2527:179322:17:18:93:525:163:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:change in investment demand, aggregate demandYtwill increase; but there will be

79:2530:179534:0:18:111:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:We conclude that while quantitative easingmayincrease risks to financial stabil-
79:2531:179614:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ity in the case that nominal rigidities allow short-run effects of monetary policy on
79:2532:179699:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate demand,  itneed nothave any  such  effect.  If the increase in the  central
79:2533:179784:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank’s balance sheet is combined with an increase in the interest rate paid on cash, or
79:2534:179871:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a tightening of macroprudential policy to a sufficient extent, it can increase aggregate
79:2535:179959:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand without any adverse consequences for financial stability.  It is particularly
79:2536:180043:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easy to achieve this outcome by combining the quantitative easing with macropruden-
79:2537:180126:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tial policy, if a suitable macroprudential instrument exists; for in our model, reduction
79:2538:180215:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ofξt+1provides an even greater disincentive to issuance of short-term debt by banks
79:2539:180298:17:18:93:485:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:than does raisingRmt+1, for a given degree of reduction in aggregate demand.
79:2540:180374:18:17:111:525:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:These results imply that quantitative easing may be a useful addition to a central
79:2541:180456:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bank’s monetary policy toolkit, even when interest-rate policy is not yet constrained
79:2542:180541:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by the effective lower bound on short-term nominal interest rates.  In the case of a
79:2543:180625:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:contractionary shockχ,the effects on aggregate demand can be offset purely through
79:2544:180707:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a  reduction  inRmt+1,if  the  lower  bound  does  not  prevent  the  size  of  rate  cut  that
79:2545:180802:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is  needed;  but  such  a  response  increases  risks  to  financial  stability  more  than  is
79:2546:180897:18:17:93:525:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:necessary.  One could alternatively counter the effects of theχshock by increasing
79:2547:180979:17:17:95:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B: ̃mt+1,while leavingRmt+1unchanged; and this would have the advantage of posing less
79:2548:181063:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of a threat to financial stability.  Even better, one could combine a somewhat larger
79:2549:181148:18:17:93:525:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increase in   ̃mt+1with a tightening of macroprudential policy, allowing the effects of
79:2550:181235:17:17:93:525:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:theχshock on aggregate demand to be offset, with even less of an increased risk to
79:2551:181317:17:45:93:291:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability, possibly none at all.
79:2552:181359:45:29:93:222:298:17:g_d0_f7:17:g_d0_f7:C:6    Conclusions
79:2553:181375:29:17:93:524:269:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:We can now assess the validity of the concerns about the consequences of quantitative
79:2554:181460:17:18:93:524:252:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing for financial stability sketched in the introduction, in the light of the model
79:2555:181546:18:17:93:524:234:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:just presented.  Our model is one in which monetary policy does indeed influence risks
79:2556:181632:17:17:93:524:217:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to financial stability; in particular, policies that loosen financial conditions, either by
79:2557:181723:17:18:93:524:200:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:lowering the central bank’s operating target for its policy rate (conventional monetary
79:2558:181810:18:17:93:524:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policy), or by relaxing reserve requirements (or other macro-prudential constraints),
79:2559:181895:17:17:93:524:165:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:should each increase the attractiveness of private issuance of “money-like” liabilities,
79:2560:181983:17:18:93:524:148:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:resulting  in  increased  leverage  and  as  a  consequence  an  increased  risk  of  serious
79:2561:182076:18:0:93:524:130:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:resource  misallocation  in  the  event  of  a  funding  crisis.   This  means  that  there  can
80:2562:182174:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:at times be a tension between the monetary policy that would be preferable strictly
80:2563:182257:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:from the standpoint of aggregate demand management and inflation stabilization, on
80:2564:182339:17:17:93:486:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the one hand, and the policy that would minimize risks to financial stability.
80:2565:182417:17:18:111:525:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:The question is whether it is correct to think of quantitative easing as a policy
80:2566:182498:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:analogous to these, and hence that poses similar risks to financial stability. Our model
80:2567:182586:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:implies that such an analogy is imperfect. A quantitative easing policy (increasing the
80:2568:182673:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:public supply of safe assets, by issuing additional safe liabilities of the central bank,
80:2569:182762:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:used to purchase assets that do not earn a similar safety premium) similarly increases
80:2570:182848:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate demand by lowering the equilibrium rate of return on non-safe assets.  But
80:2571:182932:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:unlike conventional monetary policy, it does this by lowering the equilibrium safety
80:2572:183016:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:premium (by making safe assets less scarce), rather than by lowering the equilibrium
80:2573:183100:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:return  on  safe  assets;  and  this  does  not  have  the  same  consequences  for  financial
80:2574:183194:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stability.  Lowering the equilibrium return on risky investments (such as the “durable
80:2575:183280:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:goods” modeled here, which one may think of as housing) by lowering the return on
80:2576:183361:17:17:93:525:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:safe assets works only insofar as theincreasedspread between the two returns that
80:2577:183442:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:would result if the return on risky investments did not also fall increases the incentive
80:2578:183531:18:17:93:524:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to finance additional risky investment by issuing safe liabilities, thus increasing the
80:2579:183618:17:17:93:524:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:leverage of the banks and the degree to which they engage in liquidity transformation;
80:2580:183704:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:this results in a reduced equilibrium return on risky investment, but not by enough
80:2581:183787:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to  fully  eliminate  the  increased  spread  that  induces  banks  to  issue  additional  safe
80:2582:183882:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:asset-backed  liabilities.   This  mechanism  necessarily  increases  the  risk  to  financial
80:2583:183976:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:stability  at  the  same  time  as  it  increases  aggregate  demand.   Quantitative  easing
80:2584:184068:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:insteaddecreasesthe  spread  between  these  two  returns,  at  least  in  the  absence  of
80:2585:184159:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:any  change  in  the  private  supply  of  safe  liabilities.   This  reduction  in  the  spread
80:2586:184255:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:reduces the incentive for private issuance of such liabilities, and reduced issuance of
80:2587:184342:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:safe asset-backed liabilities by banks offsets some of the reduction in the spread, but
80:2588:184429:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:does not completely eliminate it as otherwise banks would not have a reason to reduce
80:2589:184514:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:their issuance.  Hence in this case the reduction in the equilibrium return on risky
80:2590:184598:18:17:93:525:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:investments is associated with areductionof the incentive for liquidity transformation
80:2591:184684:17:17:93:268:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by banks, rather than an increase.
80:2592:184718:17:18:111:525:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Similarly, quantitative easing increases the total supply of safe assets and so re-
80:2593:184801:18:17:93:524:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:duces the safety premium; but unlike a reduction in reserve requirements (or relax-
80:2594:184884:17:17:93:524:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ation of macroprudential policy), it achieves this by increasing the public supply of
80:2595:184969:17:0:93:524:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:safe assets (and actually reducing the incentive for private issuance), rather than by
81:2596:185057:0:18:93:524:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increasing the incentive that banks have to finance risky investment by issuing safe
81:2597:185141:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:asset-backed liabilities.  Again the consequences for the degree of liquidity transfor-
81:2598:185228:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:mation by the banking sector, and hence the risk to financial stability, are entirely
81:2599:185313:17:18:93:139:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:different.
81:2600:185323:18:17:111:525:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Likewise, it is true that quantitative easing eases financial conditions by reducing
81:2601:185407:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the spread between the required return on risky investments and the return on safe
81:2602:185489:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:assets; but this does not mean that risk premia are “artificially” reduced in a way that
81:2603:185577:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:distorts incentives for prudent behavior, leading to excessive risk-taking. In the model
81:2604:185665:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:presented here, quantitative easing reduces the safety premium, but because the pub-
81:2605:185749:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:lic supply of safe assets for private investors to hold is increased,  and not because
81:2606:185835:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:anyone  is  misled  into  under-estimating  the  degree  of  risk  involved  in  undertaking
81:2607:185927:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risky investments.  Moreover, the reduced spread reduces the incentive for private is-
81:2608:186013:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:suance of safe liabilities, and instead favors financing of investment through issuance
81:2609:186100:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of non-safe liabilities, which is desirable on financial stability grounds.  Rather than
81:2610:186188:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:threatening financial stability by encouraging more risk-taking, it favors it by encour-
81:2611:186276:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:aging forms of financing that reduce the magnitude of the distortions associated with
81:2612:186361:18:17:93:174:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a funding crisis.
81:2613:186378:17:17:111:525:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:In our model, we can compare the effects of three alternative policies that can in-
81:2614:186461:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:crease aggregate demand by easing financial conditions:  reducing the central bank’s
81:2615:186545:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:operating target for the nominal interest rate on safe assets (conventional monetary
81:2616:186629:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:policy,  on  the  assumption  that  the  zero  lower  bound  does  not  yet  preclude  such
81:2617:186720:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:easing),  relaxing reserve requirements (or other macro-prudential constraints),  and
81:2618:186805:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:quantitative easing.  We find that among these, quantitative easing is the policy that
81:2619:186891:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:increases risks to financial stability the least, for any given degree of increase in aggre-
81:2620:186983:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:gate demand.  Not only does quantitative easing make it possible for a central bank
81:2621:187066:18:17:93:524:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to increase aggregate demand even when conventional monetary policy is constrained
81:2622:187148:17:17:93:524:256:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:by the zero lower bound on nominal interest rates, but it is possible, at least in prin-
81:2623:187236:17:18:93:524:239:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:ciple, to increase aggregate demand without the collateral effect of an increased risk
81:2624:187322:18:17:93:524:221:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to  financial  stability,  if  the  increased  supply  of  safe  liabilities  by  the  central  bank
81:2625:187422:17:17:93:524:204:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:is  combined  with  a  sufficient  tightening  of  macroprudential  measures.   (The  latter
81:2626:187514:17:18:93:524:187:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:measures would by themselves reduce aggregate demand;  but when combined with
81:2627:187591:18:17:93:524:169:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:quantitative easing, the net effect is an increase in aggregate demand, even when the
81:2628:187676:17:17:93:524:152:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:degree of macroprudential tightening is enough to fully offset any increase in risks to
81:2629:187763:17:0:93:385:135:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:financial stability as a result of the balance-sheet policy.)
82:2630:187826:0:18:111:525:707:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:This indicates that a concern for the effects of monetary policy on financial sta-
82:2631:187908:18:17:93:524:689:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:bility need not preclude using quantitative easing to stimulate aggregate demand in
82:2632:187991:17:17:93:524:672:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:circumstances where (as in the US in the aftermath of the recent crisis) conventional
82:2633:188076:17:18:93:524:655:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:monetary policy is constrained by the zero lower bound.  In fact,  the fact that de-
82:2634:188160:18:17:93:524:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:mand stimulus through quantitative easing poses smaller risks to financial stability
82:2635:188244:17:17:93:524:620:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:than demand stimulus through lowering short-term nominal interest rates suggests
82:2636:188324:17:18:93:524:603:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:that balance-sheet policy may be a useful tool of monetary stabilization policy even
82:2637:188408:18:17:93:524:585:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:when a central bank is far from the zero lower bound.  In the model presented here,
82:2638:188491:17:17:93:524:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate demand stimulus achieved by lowering nominal interest rates increases the
82:2639:188574:17:18:93:524:551:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:risk to financial stability more than would a quantitative easing policy that is equally
82:2640:188662:18:17:93:524:533:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:effective  in  increasing  aggregate  demand.   This  implies  that  (even  if  macropruden-
82:2641:188754:17:17:93:524:516:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:tial  policy  is  unavailable  or  ineffective)  it  should  be  possible  to  increase  aggregate
82:2642:188852:17:18:93:524:499:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:demand without increasing the risk to financial stability by combining expansionary
82:2643:188935:18:17:93:524:481:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:balance-sheet policy with an appropriate size ofincreasein the policy rate.  In such
82:2644:189019:17:17:93:524:464:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:a case, conventional monetary policy would essentially be used for macroprudential
82:2645:189101:17:18:93:524:447:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:purposes (to control the risk to financial stability) while balance-sheet policy is used
82:2646:189189:18:17:93:221:429:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:for demand stabilization.
82:2647:189214:17:17:111:525:412:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:A:Further study of the effects of quantitative easing policies would therefore seem to
82:2648:189298:17:18:93:524:395:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:be warranted, not simply for the sake of having a more effective policy toolkit for use
82:2649:189385:18:17:93:524:377:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:the next time that conventional policy is again constrained by the zero lower bound,
82:2650:189469:17:17:93:524:360:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:but  also,  arguably,  in  order  to  improve  the  conduct  of  stabilization  policy  under
82:2651:189562:17:18:93:524:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:more  normal  circumstances  as  well.   The  availability  of  this  additional  dimension
82:2652:189653:18:17:93:524:325:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:of  monetary  policy  is  particularly  likely  to  be  of  use  under  circumstances  where
82:2653:189745:17:17:93:524:308:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:additional monetary stimulus through interest-rate reduction is unattractive owing
82:2654:189827:17:18:93:524:291:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:to concerns about financial stability.  Such a situation could easily arise even when
82:2655:189912:18:0:93:379:273:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:B:interest rates are well above their effective lower bound.
